shall not be longer than three (3) days.
   D.   Before the temporary permit may be issued, the applicant or owner of
the premises must show proof of valid existing dram shop insurance to cover any
liability which may be incurred on account of said event. (1990 Code § 11.310)
3-2-25: INSPECTIONS:
All licensees are hereby required to make available for inspection by the Local
Liquor Control Commissioner and the Kankakee County Sheriff's Department the
premises where liquor is sold, served or consumed. (1990 Code § 11.326; amd.
2019 Code)
3-2-26: RESPONSIBILITY FOR VIOLATIONS:
   A.   If the owner of the licensed premises or any person from whom the
licensee derives the right to possession of such premises, or the agent of such
owner or person, shall knowingly permit the licensee to use the licensed
premises in violation of the terms of this chapter, the owner, agent or other
person shall be deemed guilty of a violation of this chapter to the same extent
as shall the licensee and shall be subject to the same punishment as the
licensee.
   B.   Every act or omission of whatsoever nature constituting a violation of
any of the provisions of this chapter by any officer, director, manager, or
agent or employee of any licensee shall be deemed and held to be the act of
such employer or licensee, and the employer or licensee shall be subject to
punishment in the same manner as if the act or omission had been done or
omitted personally. (1990 Code § 11.325)
3-2-27: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
   A.   Grounds: The Local Liquor Control Commissioner may suspend or revoke
any license issued under this chapter for any one or more of the following
reasons:
      1.   Violation of the laws of the United States government, the laws of
the State of Illinois or any of the ordinances of the Village. (1990 Code §
11.316)
      2.   Knowingly permitting any violation of this Code upon the premises
for which the license is issued. (1990 Code § 11.316; amd. 2019 Code)
      3.   Wilfully making any false statements as to a material fact in the
application for a license.
      4.   Failure of the licensee, for any cause whatsoever, to operate and
maintain a place of business at the location and on the premises pursuant to
the purpose for which the license was issued under this chapter. (1990 Code §
11.316)
      5.   Failure to keep any license issued hereunder continuously in effect
and use in an operative business during the period for which it is issued, and
when said business is abandoned, closed or for any reason becomes inoperative
for a period of thirty (30) days or more, the Local Liquor Control
Commissioner, in his discretion, may revoke said license. (1990 Code § 11.316;
amd. 2019 Code)
      6.   Any provision of the Illinois Video Gaming Act, 230 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 40/1 et seq., any of the rules, regulations, opinions and
administrative decisions of the Illinois Department of Revenue and/or the
Illinois Gaming Board concerning or related to the Illinois Video Gaming Act,
or any provisions of subsection 5-3C-1A of this Code. (Ord. 12-11, 8-6-2012)
   B.   Notice And Hearing: Notice of suspension or revocation shall be given
to the licensee after due consideration by the Local Liquor Control
Commissioner, and said suspension or revocation shall be effective unless the
licensee demands in writing a request for a hearing within three (3) days after
receiving notice. (1990 Code § 11.316.1)
3-2-28: APPEALS:
Pursuant to section 7-9 of the Illinois Liquor Control Act, 235 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/7-9, all appeals from the decisions of the Local Liquor
Control Commissioner shall be limited to a review of the official record of
proceedings of such Liquor Control Commissioner. (Ord. 97-4, 3-17-1997)
3-2-29: PENALTIES:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall violate any of the provisions of this
chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than twenty five dollars
($25.00) nor more than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for each offense, and
each day on which a violation occurs or continues shall be considered a
separate offense. Revocation or suspension of a license may be in addition to
the imposition of a fine or other penalty for violation of any of the
provisions of this chapter, and such revocation or suspension shall be no
defense to a prosecution for such violation. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord.
97-4, 3-17-1997)
CHAPTER 3
VIDEO GAMING TERMINALS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Definition
3-3-2: Sticker Required
3-3-3: Application For Sticker
3-3-4: Term Of Sticker
3-3-5: Posting Sticker
3-3-1: DEFINITION:
The term "video gaming terminal", when used in this chapter, means any
electronic video game machine that, upon insertion of cash, electronic cards or
vouchers, or any combination thereof, is available to play or simulate the play
of a video game including, but not limited to, video poker, line up, and
blackjack, as authorized by the Illinois Gaming Board utilizing a video display
and microprocessors in which the player may receive free games or credits that
can be redeemed for cash. The term does not include a machine that directly
dispenses coins, cash, or tokens or is for amusement purposes only. (Ord. 12-
12, 8-6-2012; amd. 2019 Code)
3-3-2: STICKER REQUIRED:
No person, firm, partnership, association or corporation shall own, conduct,
manage or operate a video gaming terminal in the Village without first having
obtained a Village sticker therefor pursuant to this chapter. (Ord. 12-12, 8-6-
2012)
3-3-3: APPLICATION FOR STICKER:
An applicant for any Village sticker under the provisions of this chapter shall
submit to the Village Clerk an application in writing, on forms provided by the
Village, along with a nonrefundable fee of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per
video gaming terminal. (Ord. 12-12, 8-6-2012)
3-3-4: TERM OF STICKER:
Each sticker issued pursuant to this chapter shall be issued for a term not to
exceed one year. (Ord. 12-12, 8-6-2012)
3-3-5: POSTING STICKER:
Every person issued any sticker in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter shall immediately affix the sticker to each individual video gaming
terminal or game and hang the sticker(s) so issued in a conspicuous place on
the premises and shall keep such sticker so posted during all of the time the
video gaming terminal(s) is/are present on the premises. (Ord. 12-12, 8-6-2012)
CHAPTER 4
AMUSEMENT DEVICES AND CENTERS
SECTION:
3-4-1: Definitions
3-4-2: Amusement Device Licensing Provisions
3-4-2-1: License Required; Separate Licenses
3-4-2-2: Application For License
3-4-2-3: Issuance Of And Restrictions On License; Contents
3-4-2-4: Transfer Of And Amendments To License
3-4-2-5: Display Of License
3-4-3: Amusement Center Licensing Provisions
3-4-3-1: License Required
3-4-3-2: Application For License
3-4-3-3: Issuance Of And Restrictions On License; Contents
3-4-3-4: Transfer Of And Amendments To License
3-4-3-5: Display Of License
3-4-4: License Fees
3-4-5: Expiration Of Licenses
3-4-6: Location Restrictions
3-4-7: Investigation Of Application
3-4-8: Renewal Of Licenses
3-4-9: False Affidavits Or Statements
3-4-10: Prohibited Practices
3-4-11: Revocation Of Licenses
3-4-12: Appeals
3-4-13: Penalties
3-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and terms are defined and
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, unless the context
clearly indicates a different meaning:
AMUSEMENT CENTER OR ARCADE: Any establishment, place, premises, structure, or
enclosure of any design or any place of business at which five (5) or more
amusement devices are located for the use or entertainment of persons
patronizing the place of business.
AMUSEMENT DEVICE OR DEVICE(S): Any amusement machine or device operated by
means of the insertion of a coin, token, slug, disc, plate, card, or similar
object, or upon payment of consideration, which operates or may be operated by
the public generally as a game, a contest or test of skill, or other amusement
of any description. An amusement device does not include cigarette, candy, or
other similar type vending machines.
EXHIBITOR: Any person conducting business at a place of business at which four
(4) or less amusement devices are located for the use or entertainment of
persons patronizing the place of business, irrespective of the ownership of the
device or devices.
GOOD MORAL CHARACTER: The owner, exhibitor, or operator has not been convicted
of a felony, a misdemeanor involving moral turpitude, or any gambling
conviction or convictions within the five (5) years next preceding the date of
the application.
OPERATOR: Any person conducting business at a place of business which is an
amusement center wherein five (5) or more amusement devices are located for the
use of entertainment of persons patronizing the place of business, irrespective
of the ownership of the devices.
OWNER: Any person possessing legal title to any amusement device. (Ord. 05-01,
2-23-2005)
3-4-2: AMUSEMENT DEVICE LICENSING PROVISIONS:
3-4-2-1: LICENSE REQUIRED; SEPARATE LICENSES:
No person, as an owner, operator, or exhibitor, shall locate, cause to be
located, or permit any amusement device in the Village unless such amusement
device is the subject of a valid license issued by the Village Clerk. A
separate license shall be required for each amusement device displayed at any
one time by any owner, operator, or exhibitor. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-2-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Application for a license to display an amusement device, as defined in section
3-4-1 of this chapter, must be made to the Village upon such forms as shall be
prepared therefor by the Village Clerk. Each applicant for an amusement device
license shall set forth the name and address of the owner of the amusement
device, the name and address of the exhibitor, the nature and address of the
place of business at which the amusement device is to be exhibited, a
description of the amusement device sought to be licensed, including the name,
make, model, and serial number of such device, and any other information as the
Village may reasonably require. There shall be filed with each application for
an amusement device license, affidavits of the owner and the exhibitor as to
their good moral character and the truth of the information set forth in the
application for the amusement device license. Applications for more than one
amusement device may be submitted on the same application form. (Ord. 05-01, 2-
23-2005)
3-4-2-3: ISSUANCE OF AND RESTRICTIONS ON LICENSE; CONTENTS:
The Village Clerk is authorized to issue amusement device licenses upon
approval by the Village Board of Trustees. The amusement device license shall
set forth the name and address of the owner of the amusement device, the name
and address of the exhibitor, the nature and address of the place of business
at which the licensed amusement device is to be located, the fiscal year for
which such license is issued, and any other information as reasonably may be
required by the Village. No amusement device license shall issue unless:
   A.   The exhibitor of the amusement device to be licensed has properly filed
the application for the amusement device license and affidavits as required in
section
3-4-2-2 of this section
3-4-2.
   B.   The fee required by section
3-4-4 of this chapter has been paid.
   C.   The Village Clerk has found that the exhibitor and owner are of good
moral character, as defined in section
3-4-1 of this chapter.
   D.   The amusement device to be licensed is not held, exhibited, or operated
contrary to the provisions of the laws of the State of Illinois, this Code, or
the requirements of this chapter.
   E.   The Village Clerk has determined that there exists no other reasonable
cause to deny the issuance of the amusement device license as required by the
laws of the State of Illinois, this Code, or the requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-2-4: TRANSFER OF AND AMENDMENTS TO LICENSE:
   A.   An amusement device license issued to an exhibitor under the provisions
of this chapter shall not be transferred to any other person until the
transferee has complied with all requirements of this chapter and has been
issued an amusement device license.
   B.   Should the exhibitor named on an amusement device license move the
business, such license may be transferred to the licensed exhibitor's new
business location.
   C.   An amusement device license may be amended for an exhibitor therein
named to change the selection of amusement devices.
   D.   A request for a transfer as provided in subsection B of this section or
an amendment as provided in subsection C of this section must be made by the
licensed exhibitor to the Village Clerk. A transfer or amendment provided in
this section shall be granted after a determination by the Village Clerk that
such transfer or amendment does not violate the laws of the State of Illinois,
this Code, or the requirements of this chapter.
   E.   Any transfer or amendment of an amusement device license, as herein
provided, shall be requested by the exhibitor on forms prescribed by the
Village Clerk.
   F.   This section is not applicable to an amusement center. (Ord. 05-01, 2-
23-2005)
3-4-2-5: DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
Each amusement device license shall be prominently displayed at the place of
business listed thereon in full view of the patrons of the business. (Ord. 05-
01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-3: AMUSEMENT CENTER LICENSING PROVISIONS:
3-4-3-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person, as an owner or operator, shall operate an amusement center at any
place of business unless such operator holds a valid amusement center license
in accordance with the requirements of this chapter for the place of business
at which such amusement center is operated. Each amusement device located
within the amusement center shall be approved in accordance with the
requirements of this chapter. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-3-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
The Village Clerk is authorized to accept applications for the issuance of
amusement center licenses. Each application for an amusement center license
shall be submitted upon a form prescribed by the Village Clerk and shall set
forth the name and address of the owner of the amusement devices, the name and
address of the operator, if not the same as the owner, the address of the place
of business which is to be the licensed amusement center, the fiscal period for
which the amusement center license is sought, and a description of the
amusement devices sought to be licensed at the amusement center, including the
name, make, model, and serial number. If the operator filing the application
for an amusement center license is a corporation, the application for an
amusement center license shall list the names of any individual, corporation,
or other entity owning the issued and outstanding shares of any class of stock
of the corporation, including the percentage of ownership. If the operator
filing the application for an amusement center license is a partnership, the
application shall list the names of all of the partners. There shall be filed
with each application for an amusement center license affidavits of the owner
and operator, if not the same as the owner, as to their good moral character
and the truth of the information provided in the application for the license.
(Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-3-3: ISSUANCE OF AND RESTRICTIONS ON LICENSE; CONTENTS:
The Village Clerk is authorized to issue amusement center licenses upon
approval by the Village Board of Trustees. Each amusement center license shall
set forth the name and address of the owner of the amusement device, the name
and address of the operator, if not the same as the owner, the address of the
place of business which is the licensed amusement center, and the fiscal year
for which such license is issued. The Village Clerk shall issue no license
unless:
   A.   The owner or operator of the amusement center to be licensed has
properly filed the application for an amusement center license and affidavits
required by section
3-4-3-2 of this section
3-4-3;
   B.   The fee required by section
3-4-4 of this chapter has been paid;
   C.   The Village Clerk has found that the owner and the operator, if not the
same as the owner, are of good moral character, as defined in section
3-4-1 of this chapter; (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
   D.   The applicant presently maintains a residence in the Village and has
maintained the residence a period of one year prior to submitting an
application; (2019 Code)
   E.   The Village Clerk has found that the amusement devices are not held,
exhibited, or operated contrary to the provisions of the laws of the State of
Illinois, this Code, or the requirements of this chapter; and
   F.   The Village Clerk has determined that there exists no other reasonable
cause to deny the issuance of the amusement center license as required by the
laws of the State of Illinois, this Code, or the requirements of this chapter.
(Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-3-4: TRANSFER OF AND AMENDMENTS TO LICENSE:
   A.   Transfer:
      1.   An amusement center license issued to an operator under the
provisions of this chapter shall not be transferred to any other person until
the transferee has complied with all requirements of this chapter and has been
issued an amusement center license by the Village Clerk.
      2.   Should the operator named on an amusement center license move his
business, such license may be transferred to the licensed operator's new
business location.
      3.   A request for a transfer, as stated in subsection A2 of this
section, must be made by the licensed operator to the Village Clerk upon forms
prescribed by the Village Clerk. A transfer shall be granted after a
determination by the Village Clerk that such transfer does not violate any laws
of the State of Illinois, this Code, the Village, or the requirements of this
chapter.
   B.   Amendments: An amusement center license may be amended to reflect
additions to the selection of amusement devices. Should the addition of
amusement devices require any additional license fee pursuant to section
3-4-4 of this chapter, then a list of the additional amusement devices must be
made seven (7) days prior to the installation of such coin amusement devices to
allow for a license amendment. Any list required by this section shall include
the name, make, model, and serial number of the amusement device. (Ord. 05-01,
2-23-2005)
3-4-3-5: DISPLAY OF LICENSE:
Each amusement center license shall be prominently displayed at the place of
business listed thereon in full view of the patrons of the licensed amusement
center. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-4: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   The fees for an amusement device license or an amusement center license
shall be as follows:
      1.   For the license of any one or more pool tables, the annual fee shall
be one hundred dollars ($100.00) per pool table.
      2.   For the license of any and all other amusement devices including,
but not limited to, one or more pinball machines, the annual fee shall be
thirty five dollars ($35.00) per machine.
      3.   For the license of any amusement center, the fee shall be one
hundred dollars ($100.00) per year. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005; amd. 2019 Code)
   B.   The amount of the license fee for an amusement device or amusement
center shall be computed and established at the time the license is approved
and issued by the Village Clerk, and the fee, or any part thereof, shall be
nonrefundable during the annual term of the license. The person in whose name
the license is issued is responsible and liable for the payment of the license
fee. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-5: EXPIRATION OF LICENSES:
Each amusement device license or amusement center license shall expire on and
shall be renewed by July 31 following the date of issuance. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-
2005)
3-4-6: LOCATION RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   No license shall be granted for any amusement device or amusement
center at a place where such amusement device will be displayed or the
amusement center will conduct business at a location that is within two hundred
feet (200') of the boundaries of a parcel of real estate occupied by any school
building, public library, park, playground, or place of worship.
   B.   An amusement center shall not be located within one thousand feet
(1,000') of the boundaries of a parcel of real estate occupied by another
amusement center.
   C.   The location or locations of an amusement center within a shopping mall
or within the boundaries of a shopping center shall not be located within one
thousand feet (1,000') of another amusement center within the same shopping
mall or shopping center.
   D.   This section shall not apply to a duly licensed amusement device or
amusement center location in existence at the time a school, public library,
park, playground, or place of worship moves or is constructed within the
distances prescribed in this section. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-7: INVESTIGATION OF APPLICATION:
It shall be the duty of the Village Clerk to require an investigation of each
application for an amusement device or amusement center license and to
determine whether or not the place of business where the license is sought to
be located is in violation of any law, and the amusement devices comply with
the laws, ordinances, and regulations applicable thereto, and to cause an
investigation of the good moral character of the persons, as defined herein.
This investigation is to be conducted by the Village President or the Kankakee
County Sheriff's Department who shall file a written report and recommendation
of such investigation with the Village Clerk. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005; amd. 2019
Code)
3-4-8: RENEWAL OF LICENSES:
   A.   All applications for the renewal of an amusement device or amusement
center license shall be submitted to the Village Clerk not earlier than thirty
(30) days, but not less than five (5) days, prior to the expiration of the
license and shall be upon forms provided by the Village Clerk. License fees
shall accompany all applications for renewal.
   B.   If an application is timely filed pursuant to the terms of this section
and no renewal license has been issued before the expiration date of the
existing license, the applicant may continue to operate under its existing
license until a renewal license is issued or until notified that no renewal
license will be issued. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-9: FALSE AFFIDAVITS OR STATEMENTS:
Any person who knowingly swears falsely in any affidavit required to be filed
under the provisions of this chapter or makes a false statement in any
application for an amusement device or amusement center license shall be guilty
of a violation of this chapter. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-10: PROHIBITED PRACTICES:
It shall be unlawful for any person:
   A.   To use slugs, tokens, plates, discs, cards, or any objects other than
United States coins to operate an amusement device, except for slugs, tokens,
plates, discs, or any other object furnished by the owner of such amusement
device at the location of the owner's amusement device for use in the owner's
machines only and having no redemption in cash value other than play or
amusement; or
   B.   To use or permit the use of any such amusement device as a gambling
device or in connection with gambling. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005)
3-4-11: REVOCATION OF LICENSES:
   A.   If at any time any licensee, or a managing officer thereof if the
licensee is a corporation, firm, partnership, or association, or the person in
charge of or managing the operation of such amusement device or amusement
center is found to be in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter or
any laws against gambling, the Village may, after a hearing of which such
licensee shall be given written notice, revoke such license. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-
2005)
   B.   If at any time there has been a breach of the peace in a one year
period at the location where said amusement device is used, and said breach of
the peace has caused any police, fire, ambulance or rescue agency or department
to respond to said breach of the peace, the Village may, after a hearing of
which such licensee shall be given written notice, revoke such license. (Ord.
05-01, 2-23-2005; amd. 2019 Code)
3-4-12: APPEALS:
   A.   Any person whose initial application for an amusement device or
amusement center license is denied or whose existing license is not renewed or
is revoked by the Village Clerk may appeal such decision to the Village Board,
provided notice of appeal in writing is submitted to the Village Clerk within
ten (10) days after receipt of such denial, revocation, or failure to renew.
   B.   The Village Board shall hear any appeal timely made within thirty (30)
days from the date such notice of appeal is received by the Village Clerk, and
the Village Board shall have the power to sustain, modify, or reverse such
decision. The Village Board's decision must be in writing and sent to the
license holder within fifteen (15) days after the hearing is concluded. The
decision of the Village Board shall be final. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005; amd. 2019
Code)
3-4-13: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined in a sum
not to exceed seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). Each day that a violation
of this chapter continues shall constitute a separate offense and shall be
punishable as such. The penalty herein provided shall be cumulative with, and
in addition to, the forfeiture of any license or right provided elsewhere in
this chapter for violation thereof. (Ord. 05-01, 2-23-2005; amd. 2019 Code)
CHAPTER 5
PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Definitions
3-5-2: Application For Permit
3-5-3: Permit Fees
3-5-4: Review Of Application; Issuance Of Permit; Recordkeeping
3-5-5: Denial Of Permit
3-5-6: Expiration Of Permit
3-5-7: Permit To Be Exhibited
3-5-8: Unlawful Use Of Permit
3-5-9: Hours Of Peddling Or Soliciting
3-5-10: Uninvited Peddling Or Soliciting
3-5-11: Suspension Or Revocation Of Permit
3-5-12: Appeals
3-5-13: Exemptions For Charitable Organizations
3-5-14: First Amendment Solicitations
3-5-15: Penalties
3-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, and their derivations, when used in
this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except
where the context clearly indicated a different meaning:
CHARITABLE: Means and includes the words patriotic, political, philanthropic,
social service, health, welfare, benevolent, educational, civic, cultural or
fraternal, either actual or purported.
CONTRIBUTIONS: Means and includes the words alms, money, subscription, property
or any donations under the guise of a loan or money or property.
PEDDLER: Any person who goes upon the premises of any private residence in the
Village, not having been invited by the occupant thereof, carrying or
transporting goods, wares, merchandise or personal property of any nature and
offering the same for sale. This definition also includes any person who only
solicits orders and, as a separate transaction, makes deliveries to purchasers
as part of the scheme to evade the provisions of this chapter.
PEDDLING: Includes all activities ordinarily performed by a peddler as
indicated under the definition of peddler of this section.
PERMIT: A copy of the permit application file, stamped by the Village Clerk,
which must be in the possession of the permittee and the employees or agents of
such permittee engaging in soliciting or peddling as provided in this chapter
at all times any individual or individuals are engaging in authorized
solicitation or peddling.
PERSON: A natural person and/or the person's employee or agent, or any firm,
corporation, association, club, society or other organization.
RESIDENCE: Means and includes every separate living unit occupied for
residential purposes by one or more persons, contained within any type of
building or structure.
SOLICITATION: Includes all activities ordinarily performed by a solicitor as
indicated under the definition of solicitor of this section.
SOLICITOR: Any person who goes upon the premises of any private residence in
the Village, not having been invited by the occupant thereof, for the purpose
of taking or attempting to take orders for the sale of goods or services,
tangible or intangible, goods, services, or other personal property of any
nature for future delivery, or for services to be performed in the future.
(Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-2: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Every person, and/or the employees or agents of such person, subject to the
provisions of this chapter shall, prior to entering upon the premises of any
private residence within the Village, file with the Village Clerk an
application for a permit in writing on a form to be furnished by the Village
Clerk, a copy of which is on file in the Village as exhibit A, which shall
provide the following information: (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013; amd. 2019 Code)
   A.   Proof of age, address and identity of the applicant, and/or the
employees or agents of such applicant, to be provided through the production of
a driver's license and, where applicable, documented proof of employment and/or
agency.
   B.   A brief description of the business or activity to be conducted.
   C.   The hours and location for which the right to peddle or solicit are
desired.
   D.   If an employee of the applicant, the name, address and telephone number
of the employer; or if acting as an agent, the name, address and telephone
number of the principal who is being represented.
   E.   A statement as to whether or not the applicant, and/or the employees or
agents of the applicant, have been convicted of a felony involving a sex
offense, trafficking in controlled substances, any violent acts against persons
or property or any offense involving fraud or misrepresentation.
   F.   A statement whether the applicant, and/or the employees or agents of
the applicant, are persons against whom a civil judgment based upon acts
involving fraud, deceit or misrepresentation has been entered.
   G.   Proof of possession of any license or permit which, under Federal,
State or local laws or regulations, the applicant, and/or the employees or
agents of the applicant, are required to have in order to conduct the proposed
business or which, under any such law or regulation, would exempt the applicant
from the licensing requirements of this chapter, said licenses and permits to
include specifically, but without limitation, an Illinois Business Tax number
issued by the Illinois Department of Revenue. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-3: PERMIT FEES:
At the time the application is filed with the Village Clerk, the applicant,
and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, shall pay a fee to cover the
cost to the Village of processing the application and investigating the facts
stated therein. The permit fee shall be twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the
applicant and twenty five dollars ($25.00) for each and every employee or agent
of the applicant. The permit will authorize solicitation Monday through
Saturday for six (6) consecutive working days between nine o'clock (9:00) A.M.
and sunset as defined by the current official time in effect in the Village.
(Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013; amd. 2019 Code)
3-5-4: REVIEW OF APPLICATION; ISSUANCE OF PERMIT; RECORDKEEPING:
   A.   Upon receipt of an application, the Village Clerk, or authorized
representative, shall have seven (7) working days to review the application as
deemed necessary to ensure the protection of the public health, safety and
general welfare.
   B.   If the Village Clerk finds the application to be satisfactory, the
Clerk shall endorse his/her approval on the application and shall, upon payment
of the prescribed fee, deliver a file stamped approval of the application to
the applicant, said file stamped copy representing the permit giving the
applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, authority to
solicit or peddle, as defined in section
3-5-1 of this chapter.
   C.   A record of all applications issued shall be maintained by the Village
Clerk for a period of two (2) years. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-5: DENIAL OF PERMIT:
   A.   Upon the Village Clerk's review of the application, the Village Clerk
may refuse to issue a permit to the applicant, and/or the employees or agents
of the applicant, under this chapter for any of the following reasons: (Ord.
13-07, 8-5-2013; amd. 2019 Code)
      1.   The location and time of solicitation or peddling would endanger the
safety and welfare of the solicitors, peddlers or their customers and/or
violate the day and time restrictions imposed by this chapter.
      2.   An investigation reveals that the applicant, and/or the employees or
agents of the applicant, falsified information on the application.
      3.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, have
been convicted of a sex offense, delivery or possession of controlled
substances, any violent acts against persons or property or any offense
involving fraud or misrepresentation.
      4.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, are
persons against whom a civil judgment has been entered based upon any acts
involving theft, fraud, deceit or misrepresentation.
      5.   There is no proof as to the authority of the applicant to serve as
an agent to the principal.
      6.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, have
had an application denied under this chapter, unless the applicant, and/or the
employees or agents of the applicant, can and do show, to the satisfaction of
the Village Clerk, that the reasons for such earlier denial no longer exist.
      7.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, have
previously been issued a permit by the Village and failed to comply with the
ordinances of the Village.
      8.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, are
unable to show proof of possession of a license or permit which, under Federal,
State or local law, they are required to have in order to conduct their
business or profession, such license or permit to include specifically, but
without limitation, an Illinois Business Tax number issued by the Illinois
Department of Revenue.
   B.   The Village Clerk's disapproval and the reasons for disapproval shall
be noted on the application, and the applicant shall be notified that his
application is disapproved and that no permit will be issued. Notice shall be
mailed to the applicant at the address shown on the application form or at the
applicant's last known address. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-6: EXPIRATION OF PERMIT:
All permits issued under the provisions of this chapter shall expire at such
date as indicated by the permit. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-7: PERMIT TO BE EXHIBITED:
Every person, and/or the employees or agents of such person, required to obtain
a permit under the provisions of this chapter shall exhibit the permit when
requested to do so by any prospective customer or any person acting under the
authority of the Village Clerk. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-8: UNLAWFUL USE OF PERMIT:
It shall be unlawful for any person, other than the permittee, and/or the
employees or agents of such permittee, to use any permit issued under the
provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-9: HOURS OF PEDDLING OR SOLICITING:
No permittee, and/or the employees or agents of such permittee, while
conducting the activities of a peddler or solicitor, whether licensed or
unlicensed, shall enter upon any private property, knock on doors or otherwise
disturb persons in their residences before the hours of nine o'clock (9:00)
A.M. and after sunset as defined by the current official time in effect on any
day activities are authorized. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013; amd. 2019 Code)
3-5-10: UNINVITED PEDDLING OR SOLICITING:
It shall be unlawful for any permittee, and/or the employees or agents of such
permittee, whether licensed or unlicensed, while conducting the business of a
peddler or solicitor, to enter upon any residential premises in the Village
where the owner, occupant or person legally in charge of the premises has
posted at the entry to the premises, or at the entry to the principal building
on the premises, a sign bearing the words "No Peddlers", "No Solicitors", or
words of similar import. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-11: SUSPENSION OR REVOCATION OF PERMIT:
   A.   Grounds: Any permit issued under this chapter may be revoked or
suspended by the Village Clerk, after notice and hearing, for any of the
following reasons:
      1.   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application.
      2.   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made by the permittee,
and/or the employees or agents of the permittee, in the course of conducting
solicitation or peddling activities.
      3.   Conducting peddling or solicitation activities contrary to the
provisions contained in the permit or in violation of the ordinances of the
Village.
      4.   The permittee, and/or the employees or agents of the permittee,
having a record of criminal conviction involving a sex offense, possession or
delivery in controlled substances, any violent acts against persons or property
or any offense involving fraud or misrepresentation.
      5.   The applicant, and/or the employees or agents of the applicant, are
persons against whom a civil judgment has been entered based upon any act
involving theft, fraud, deceit or misrepresentation.
      6.   Conducting peddling or solicitation activities in such a manner as
to create a public nuisance constituting a breach of the peace and/or
endangering the health, safety or general welfare of the public.
   B.   Notice And Hearing: Notice of a hearing for revocation of a permit
issued under this chapter shall be provided in writing and shall set forth
specifically the grounds for the proposed revocation and the time and place of
the hearing. Notice shall be mailed, postage prepaid, to the permittee at the
address shown on the permit application. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-12: APPEALS:
   A.   Any person aggrieved by the action or decision of the Village Clerk to
deny, suspend or revoke a permit applied for under the provisions of this
chapter shall have the right to appeal such action or decision to the Mayor and
Village Board of Trustees within fifteen (15) days after the notice of the
action or decision has been mailed to the permittee's address as shown on the
permit application form.
   B.   An appeal shall be taken by filing in person with the Village Clerk a
written statement setting forth the grounds for the appeal.
   C.   The Village Clerk shall transmit the written statement to the Mayor and
Village Board of Trustees within ten (10) days of its receipt, and the Mayor
shall set a time and place for a hearing on the appeal.
   D.   A hearing shall be set not later than thirty (30) days from the date of
receipt of the appellant's written statement.
   E.   Notice of the time and place of the hearing shall be given to the
appellant in the same manner as provided for the mailing of notice of action or
decision.
   F.   The decision of the Mayor and Village Board of Trustees on the appeal
shall be final and binding on all parties concerned. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-13: EXEMPTIONS FOR CHARITABLE ORGANIZATIONS:
   A.   Any person and/or individuals or groups identified as "charitable", as
defined in section
3-5-1 of this chapter, are exempt from compliance with the terms of this
chapter save the provision restricting the hours of solicitation and/or
peddling.
   B.   Any person, and/or the employees or agents of such person, claiming to
be legally exempt from the regulations set forth in this chapter, or from the
payment of an application fee, shall, at the time of application, cite to the
Village Clerk the statute or other legal authority under which exemption is
claimed and shall present to the Village Clerk proof of qualification for such
exemption. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
3-5-14: FIRST AMENDMENT SOLICITATIONS:
Persons soliciting for causes protected by the First Amendment of the United
States Constitution shall procure a permit without payment of the prescribed
fee and shall be restricted as to hours of solicitation, that being daylight.
(2019 Code)
3-5-15: PENALTIES:
   A.   Fine; Imprisonment: Any violation of this chapter may be punishable by
a fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00), or by imprisonment for a term not to exceed
thirty (30) days, or both. If the person has been convicted of a violation of
this chapter within the previous period of one year, the person shall be fined
not less than two hundred dollars ($200.00) or imprisoned for not more than
ninety (90) days, or both.
   B.   Community Service: In lieu of or in addition to the penalties provided
in this section, a person in violation of this chapter may be required to
perform community service work as prescribed by the court.
   C.   Civil Remedies: In addition to any criminal enforcement, the Village or
any individual resident may pursue any available civil remedies deemed
appropriate and necessary, including specifically, but without limitation to,
injunctive relief. (Ord. 13-07, 8-5-2013)
CHAPTER 6
SCAVENGERS
SECTION:
3-6-1: License Required
3-6-2: Application For License; Fee
3-6-3: Bond And Insurance Requirements
3-6-4: Term Of License
3-6-5: Vehicle Requirements
3-6-6: Disposal Of Refuse
3-6-7: Penalty
3-6-1: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person, firm or corporation shall engage in the business of scavenger or the
collection or disposal of refuse or garbage, including animal, human or
vegetable refuse, or offal, other than collecting such from commercial
establishments only, without first having secured a license therefor. (1990
Code § 11.501)
3-6-2: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE; FEE:
Application for such license shall be made to the Village Clerk and shall be
referred to the Village Board of Trustees. No such license shall be issued
except on order of the Board of Trustees. The fee for such license shall be
fifty dollars ($50.00) per year per truck. (1990 Code §§ 11.502, 11.507; amd.
2019 Code)
3-6-3: BOND AND INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Bond:
      1.   No scavenger license shall be issued unless the applicant therefor
shall first file a performance bond, with sureties to be approved by the
Village Board of Trustees, in the sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), with
the Village as beneficiary, conditioned upon the licensee continuing to
properly operate the business of scavenger for the period covered by the
license on the following terms:
         a.   The licensee will have at least one vehicle in operation in
collecting garbage.
         b.   The licensee will collect garbage or refuse from each and every
resident of the Village requesting such service; provided, that such resident
or residents pay the established fee within thirty (30) days from the date of
billing for service rendered.
         c.   The collection will be made of all garbage and refuse properly
placed in suitable containers of thirty (30) gallons' or less capacity, which
container or containers must be placed by the resident in the alley, but if
there is no alley abutting the property of the resident, then at the curb or
curb line of such property; provided, that the resident shall not be delinquent
in payment as hereinbefore provided.
         d.   Collection of such garbage or refuse shall be made between the
hours of seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and six o'clock (6:00) P.M. of the day or
days of the week selected by the licensee; provided, that once such day or days
of the week is/are selected, the licensee shall regularly make collection on
those day or days, and in the event the days selected fall on a legal holiday,
then the collection shall be made on the day following the holiday.
         e.   The term garbage or refuse does not include such materials as
concrete, trees, brush, bricks, sand, dirt, building materials, lumber or
similar materials.
         f.   The licensee will comply with all ordinance provisions relating
to the business and will properly dispose of all garbage and refuse collected.
         g.   The fee established at the start of the license year for garbage
and refuse collection shall not be increased during the license year without
the consent of the Village President and Board of Trustees.
         h.   A failure to comply with the provisions hereof because of
conditions, acts or occurrences beyond the control of the licensee, or
mechanical failure of equipment repaired or replaced promptly as possible,
shall not be considered a breach of these conditions.
      2.   Provided, that in lieu of such bond, the licensee may deposit cash
or direct general obligations of the Federal, State or Village government, in
the sum of one thousand dollars ($1,000.00), with Village Clerk; such deposits
to be returned upon compliance with the conditions of this subsection. (1990
Code § 11.505)
   B.   Insurance: Subsequent to the effective date hereof, no license shall be
issued under the provisions of this chapter unless the applicant for such
license has first been submitted a certificate by an insurer duly authorized to
issue such policies in the State of Illinois. Such certificate shall show that
the applicant for a license has public liability insurance coverage covering
operation within the Village and that the same shall not be canceled without at
least ten (10) days' notice to the Village Clerk. Upon the cancellation or
expiration without renewal of such insurance, the license issued hereunder to
the insured shall be void. Such insurance shall be in the amount of not less
than fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) per person insured, not less than one
hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) for all personal injuries in any one
accident and not less than fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) for property
damage in any one accident. (1990 Code § 11.506; amd. 2019 Code)
3-6-4: TERM OF LICENSE:
Each license granted hereunder, to be effective on or after May 1, 1990, shall
be for the term from May 1 until the following April 30. Any applicant for a
license must pay the annual fee regardless of the time when the license is
issued, and no refunds will be made, and no fees will be prorated. (1990 Code §
11.508)
3-6-5: VEHICLE REQUIREMENTS:
Any vehicle used by the scavenger shall be watertight and equipped with covers
for such portions as are used for the transportation of refuse. (1990 Code §
11.503; amd. 2019 Code)
3-6-6: DISPOSAL OF REFUSE:
It shall be unlawful for any scavenger to dispose of or store any refuse in any
place within the Village limits or within two (2) miles thereof, except with
the permission of the Village Board of Trustees. (1990 Code § 11.504)
3-6-7: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter shall
be fined not less than one dollar ($1.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00) for each offense. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1990
Code § 11.509; amd. 2019 Code)
CHAPTER 7
SEXUALLY ORIENTED BUSINESSES
SECTION:
3-7-1: Definitions
3-7-2: Registration Required
3-7-3: Location Restrictions
3-7-4: Prohibitions
3-7-5: Stage, Separation And Railing Requirements
3-7-6: Gratuities
3-7-7: Notice Of Select Rules
3-7-8: Age Limitation
3-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the words and phrases used in this chapter
shall have the following meanings unless otherwise clearly indicated by the
context:
ADULT BOOKSTORE: An establishment, having as a substantial or significant
portion of its sales or stock in trade, in books, films, video cassettes
(whether viewing off premises or on premises), or magazines and other
periodicals which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on
matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or
specified anatomical areas, as defined in this section.
ADULT CABARET: A cabaret, bar or dance hall which features topless dancers, go-
go dancers, exotic dancers, strippers, male or female impersonators, or similar
entertainers.
ADULT ENTERTAINMENT: Any exhibition of any adult oriented motion picture, live
performance, display or dance of any type, which has as a significant or
substantial portion of such performance any actual or simulated performing of
specified sexual activities or exhibition and viewing of specified anatomical
areas, removal of articles of clothing or appearing unclothed, pantomime,
modeling, or any other personal service offered customers.
ADULT MINI-MOTION PICTURE THEATER: An enclosed building with a capacity of less
than fifty (50) persons regularly used for presenting material distinguished or
characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to
specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas, as defined in this
section, for observation by patrons therein.
ADULT MOTION PICTURE THEATER: An enclosed building with a capacity of fifty
(50) or more persons regularly used for presenting material having as a
dominant theme or presenting material distinguished or characterized by an
emphasis on matter depicting, describing, or relating to specified sexual
activities or specified anatomical areas, as defined in this section, for
observation by patrons therein.
PERSON: Any individual, partnership, corporation, association, proprietorship,
or other legal entity.
RELIGIOUS INSTITUTION: A building in which persons regularly assemble for
religious worship intended primarily for purposes connected with such worship
or for propagating a particular form of religious belief.
SEXUALLY ORIENTED BUSINESS: Any premises to which the public, patrons or
members are invited or admitted and which is so physically arranged as to
provide booths, cubicles, rooms, compartments, or stalls separate from the
common areas of the premises for the purpose of viewing adult oriented motion
pictures, or wherein an entertainer provides adult entertainment to a member of
the public, or a patron, when such adult entertainment is held, conducted,
operated or maintained for a profit, direct or indirect. A sexually oriented
business further includes, without being limited to, any adult bookstores,
adult motion picture theaters, adult mini-motion picture establishments, adult
cabarets, adult entertainment studios or any premises that is physically
arranged and used as such, whether advertised or represented as an adult
entertainment studio, rap studio, exotic dance studio, encounter studio,
sensitivity studio, modeling studio or any other term of like import.
SPECIFIED ANATOMICAL AREAS: A. Less than completely and opaquely covered:
      1.   Human genitals;
      2.   Pubic region;
      3.   Buttocks;
      4.   Female breasts below a point immediately above the top of the
areola; and
   B.   Human male genitals in a discernibly turgid state, even if completely
or opaquely covered.
SPECIFIED SEXUAL ACTIVITIES: A. Human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation
or arousal.
   B.   Acts of human masturbation, sexual intercourse or sodomy.
   C.   Fondling or erotic touching of human genitals, pubic region, buttock or
female breasts. (Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007; amd. 2019 Code)
3-7-2: REGISTRATION REQUIRED:
The owner of a building or premises, his agent for the purpose of managing,
controlling or collecting rents, or any other person managing or controlling a
building or premises, any part of which contains an adult use, shall register
the following information with the Village Clerk:
   A.   The address of the premises.
   B.   The name of the owner of the premises and names of the beneficial
owners if the property is in a land trust.
   C.   The address of the owner and the beneficial owners.
   D.   The name of the business or establishment.
   E.   The name(s) and address(es) of the owner, beneficial owner or the major
stockholders of the business or establishment.
   F.   The date of initiation of the sexually oriented business.
   G.   If the premises or building is leased, a copy of said lease must be
attached. (Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007)
3-7-3: LOCATION RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Sexually oriented businesses are permitted in an Industrial District;
provided, that:
      1.   No person shall operate or cause to be operated a sexually oriented
business within one thousand feet (1,000') of the property boundary of a
preexisting:
         a.   Public or private elementary or secondary school; or
         b.   Licensed daycare center; or
         c.   Place of religious worship.
      2.   No person shall operate or cause to be operated a sexually oriented
business within five hundred feet (500') of the property boundary of a
preexisting:
         a.   Public park and/or community center;
         b.   Residential Zoning District; or
         c.   Another sexually oriented business.
   B.   For the purpose of this section, measurements shall be made in a
straight line, without regard to intervening structures or objects, from the
nearest portion of the building or structure used as a part of the premises
where the sexually oriented business is conducted to the nearest property line
of the other specified use, or the centerline of the designated roadways. (Ord.
07-07, 7-2-2007)
3-7-4: PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   Hours Of Operation: No sexually oriented business shall be open between
the hours of one o'clock (1:00) A.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. on any given
day.
   B.   Exterior Display: No sexually oriented business shall be conducted in
any manner that permits the observation of any material depicting, describing
or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas from
any public way or from any property not registered as an adult use. This
subsection shall apply to any display, decoration, sign, show window or other
opening.
   C.   Liquor: No liquor license shall be issued and no liquor shall be sold
or consumed on the premises of any sexually oriented businesses on any calendar
day on which adult entertainment is provided at the licensed establishment.
(Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007)
3-7-5: STAGE, SEPARATION AND RAILING REQUIREMENTS:
Entertainers identified in the definition of "adult cabaret" in section
3-7-1 of this chapter or similar entertainers shall perform upon a stage
elevated at least eighteen inches (18") above floor level. All parts of the
stage, or a clearly designated area thereof within which entertainers perform,
shall be a distance of at least six feet (6') from all parts of a clearly
designated area in which patrons may be present. The stage area, or the clearly
designated area thereof within which entertainers perform, shall be separated
from the area in which patrons may be located by a barrier or railing, the top
of which is at least four feet (4') above floor level. Entertainers shall
additionally stay at least six feet (6') from other entertainers on stage.
(Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007)
3-7-6: GRATUITIES:
No patron of a sexually oriented business shall offer, and no employee of a
sexually oriented business having performed on any cabaret stage shall accept,
any form of tip or gratuity offered directly or personally to the employee by
any patron. Rather, all tips and gratuities to adult establishment employees
performing on any cabaret stage shall be placed into a receptacle provided for
receipt of such tips and gratuities by the sexually oriented business. (Ord.
07-07, 7-2-2007)
3-7-7: NOTICE OF SELECT RULES:
A sign at least two feet by two feet (2' x 2'), with letters at least one inch
(1") high, shall be conspicuously displayed on or adjacent to every cabaret
stage stating: (Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007)
THIS ESTABLISHMENT IS REGULATED BY THE VILLAGE OF CHEBANSE. PERFORMERS AND
ENTERTAINERS ARE:
1. NOT PERMITTED TO ENGAGE IN ANY TYPE OF PROHIBITED SEXUAL CONDUCT.
2. NOT PERMITTED TO ACCEPT ANY TIPS DIRECTLY OR PERSONALLY FROM PATRONS. ANY
SUCH TIPS MUST BE PLACED INTO THE RECEPTACLE PROVIDED BY MANAGEMENT.
3. NOT PERMITTED TO APPEAR NUDE OR IN ANY STATE OF UNDRESS PROHIBITED AND AS
DEFINED BY THE VILLAGE.
(Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007; amd. 2019 Code)
3-7-8: AGE LIMITATION:
No licensee shall permit any person under the age of eighteen (18) upon the
premises. (Ord. 07-07, 7-2-2007; amd. 2019 Code)
TITLE 4
HEALTH, SANITATION AND ENVIRONMENT
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
4-1-1: Nuisances Enumerated
4-1-2: Inspection And Investigation Of Possible Nuisance Conditions
4-1-3: Abatement Provisions
4-1-4: Penalties
4-1-1: NUISANCES ENUMERATED:
Each of the following acts, activities or conduct is hereby declared to be a
nuisance within the limits of the Village:
   A.   Common Law Nuisances: To commit any offense which is a nuisance
according to the common law of the land or made such by the Statutes of the
State of Illinois.
   B.   Offensive Odors: To conduct any business or use any premises as to
create such an offensive smell as may taint the air and render it unwholesome
or disagreeable in the neighborhood.
   C.   Offensive Premises:
      1.   To cause or suffer the carcass of any animal or vegetable matter,
slops, swill, suds, garbage, filth, stable drippings or offal or noisome
substance of any kind to be collected or deposited or to remain in any place in
the Village to the prejudice of others.
      2.   For any person to permit any slops, swill, garbage, stable
drippings, offal, filth, refuse, or animal or vegetable matter, which is liable
to become putrid or offensive or injurious to health, to remain on any premises
or any place for a longer period than twelve (12) hours at a time.
      3.   To keep or suffer to be kept in a foul, offensive, nauseous or
filthy condition, any chicken coop, cow house, stable, cellar, vault, drain,
privy, sewer or sink upon any premises, railroad car, building, yard or
grounds.
   D.   Offensive Animal Houses And Enclosures: To own, use or keep any yard,
pen, place, railroad car or premises in or upon which cattle or other animals
shall be confined or kept, or keep any fowl, cattle or animals, so as to be
offensive to those residing in the vicinity or an annoyance to others.
   E.   Privies: To erect or maintain any privy within the Village.
   F.   Offensive Businesses:
      1.   To locate and carry on any packing house, rendery, tallow chandlery,
glue or bone factory, soap factory or tannery within the limits of the Village
and within the distance of one mile outside the Village limits.
      2.   To erect, continue or use any building or other place for the
exercise of any trade, employment or manufacture which, by occasion of noxious
exhalations, offensive smells or otherwise, is offensive or dangerous to the
health of individuals or of the public.
      3.   To slaughter or kill any cattle, hogs or sheep, or keep, maintain or
use in the Village any house or place in which the business of slaughtering any
of said animals may be carried on.
   G.   Offensive, Dangerous Parking Of Certain Vehicles: To park or cause to
be parked any semitrailer or tractor on any premises, street or alley in the
Village if such parking is offensive or dangerous to the health or safety of
individuals or of the public.
   H.   Depositing Offensive Substances:
      1.   To deposit any nightsoil, dead animal or other filthy, offensive or
noisome substance upon any lot, street, alley, highway, park or other place.
      2.   To throw, drop or deposit any paper cup, carton, plate or other
container upon a sidewalk, crosswalk, roadway or any part of any public street
or public building which is offensive or injurious to the public.
   I.   Water Pollution:
      1.   To throw or deposit, or cause to be thrown or deposited, any offal
or other offensive matter or the carcass of any animal in any watercourse,
pond, spring, creek or well in or which flows through the Village.
      2.   To corrupt or render unwholesome or injure the water of any drinking
hydrant, spring, stream, pond or lake to the injury and prejudice of others.
      3.   To obstruct or pollute any watercourse or source of water supply in
the Village.
   J.   Stagnant Water:
      1.   To obstruct any watercourse, ravine or gutter so as to cause water
to stagnate therein or to permit foul or stagnant water to stand upon any
premises to the prejudice of others.
      2.   To allow water to accumulate and remain in a pond or ponds, either
wholly or partly within the limits of any private property, for a period of
more than ten (10) consecutive days. For the purpose of this subsection J2, the
term "pond" shall be considered to mean any exposed surface of water not less
than one hundred (100) square feet in area which has accumulated either by
natural or artificial means in any depression or connected series of
depressions of excavations, whether existing naturally or created artificially.
      3.   To permit any stagnant pool of water to remain or exist on any
property where the condition is a threat to public health.
   K.   Air Pollution: To allow or permit any dense smoke, fly ash or soot to
come or be emitted from any fire, chimney, engine, oil burner or other agency
within the limits of the Village. Such nuisance may be summarily abated by whom
the Village President and Board of Trustees may authorize for such purposes.
Such abatement may be in addition to the fine provided for a violation of this
section.
   L.   Weeds And Grass As Fire Hazards: Suffering grass, leaves, underbrush or
other combustible matter to be collected or deposited or to remain on premises
in such quantities and in such condition as to materially increase the danger
to property of others from fires.
   M.   Open Burning: To cause or allow on any premises, street or alley, the
burning of paper, leaves or other matter unless supervised by the person so
doing until the fire is completely extinguished.
   N.   Expectorating In Public: To spit or expectorate on any public sidewalk,
street or other public place or floor or walk or any public vehicle or hall or
any public building.
   O.   Noisy Conditions:
      1.   To conduct any building operations or to operate any steam shovels,
pneumatic hammers, steam or electric hoists or other apparatus, the use of
which is attended with loud or unusual noise, during the hours set out in
section
9-2-4 of this Code.
      2.   To use any building, or permit the use of the same, or rent the same
to be used for any business or employment or for any purpose of pleasure or
recreation if such use shall, from its noise or boisterous nature, disturb or
destroy the peace of the neighborhood in which such building or premises is
situated or be dangerous or detrimental to health.
   P.   Unsightly Premises:
      1.   To permit or maintain an unsightly yard or premises where there is
an accumulation or deposit of any vehicle, equipment, material of any nature,
waste or earth.
      2.   To maintain an unsightly yard or area where junk, wrecked or
disabled automobiles, trucks or equipment, or other such matter, is allowed to
accumulate.
   Q.   Dangerous Premises: To permit any building, structure or place to
remain in such a condition as to be dangerous to the public health in any way.
   R.   Obstructing Public Ways: To obstruct or encroach upon public highways,
private ways, streets, alleys and commons.
   S.   Any fence found to be in violation of Title 9, Chapter 5 by the
Director of Building and Zoning and/or a majority vote of the Village Board.
(1990 Code §§ 13.403, 13.404, 13.406, 16.101; amd. 2019 Code; Ord. 23-08, 11-
20-2023)
4-1-2: INSPECTION AND INVESTIGATION OF POSSIBLE NUISANCE CONDITIONS:
When an existence of a public nuisance is brought to the attention of the
Village, the Village building inspector shall cause an inspection and
investigation to be made and to determine whether removal is necessary. (2019
Code)
4-1-3: ABATEMENT PROVISIONS:
   A.   Notice To Abate: The Village building inspector shall, after inspection
and investigating under the provisions of section
4-1-2 of this chapter, cause a notice in writing to be served upon the person,
corporation or entity found to be responsible for the existence of the
nuisance. The notice shall require the person, entity, or corporation
responsible to abate the nuisance within ten (10) days from the receipt of the
notice. If personal service of the notice cannot be made, then such notice
shall be left at the residence or usual place of business of the person found
to be responsible. The notice shall indicate the date of the inspection and
investigation, and the hours and location where the inspection was made. The
notice shall set forth what the nuisance consists of and indicate the abatement
or remedy required.
   B.   Failure To Abate; Abatement By Village; Costs: After the expiration of
ten (10) days from the time the notice is served, if the nuisance is not abated
or other remedy made as required, it may be done under the direction of the
Village building inspector, and all costs of so doing to remedy the abatement
shall be collected from the person, corporation or entity who is responsible
for the nuisance with a penalty of ten percent (10%) of such costs.
   C.   Emergency Abatement: If a nuisance constitutes an emergency, the time
for abatement may be reduced by the Village in the notices which specify that
the emergency exists.
   D.   Responsibility Of Owner, Agent Or Occupant: When any nuisance, or
anything likely to become a nuisance, may be found upon any premises, and the
person, corporation or entity causing such nuisance is unknown or cannot be
found, the owner, agent or occupant of the premises shall be notified by the
Village to abate the same. If such owner, agent or occupant whose duty it is
hereby made to abate such nuisance shall not promptly comply with such notice,
he shall be subject to the penalty provided in this chapter.
   E.   Special Lien Authorization: The costs and expenses incurred by the
Village to abate any public nuisance may be made a lien on the property on
which any such public nuisance is located pursuant to, and to the fullest
extent provided by, Illinois law. (2019 Code)
4-1-4: PENALTIES:
   A.   Fines: Any person, firm, partnership or corporation who shall violate
any of the provisions of this chapter shall be fined not less than fifty
dollars ($50.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) in the
case of a first offense and shall be fined not less than twenty five dollars
($25.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each and every
subsequent offense. Each and every day that such nuisance shall remain in
existence shall constitute a separate offense. (1990 Code § 16.102; amd. 2019
Code)
   B.   Injunction: In the event any violation is of a continuing nature, the
Village building inspector is hereby authorized to seek an injunction in the
Circuit Court to enjoin any such nuisance, and the building inspector shall
bring said action in the name of the Village. (1990 Code § 16.103)
CHAPTER 2
FOOD DEALERS
SECTION:
4-2-1: Definitions
4-2-2: Licensing Requirements
4-2-3: Unwholesome, Adulterated Food
4-2-4: Sanitary Conditions
4-2-5: Penalty
4-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the
meanings ascribed to them in this section:
FOOD: Includes beverages.
FOOD DEALER: Means and includes every person, firm or corporation engaged in
conducting or operating any business for the storage, handling, preparation or
sale of food or drink intended for human consumption. (1990 Code §§ 13.301,
13.310)
4-2-2: LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any food dealer to engage in
or do business in the Village without having first secured a license therefor.
   B.   Application For License; Fee: All applications for a license shall be
made in compliance with the general provisions of this Code relating thereto
and shall state the kind of food intended to be sold or handled. The annual fee
for such license shall be ten dollars ($10.00). (1990 Code § 13.302)
   C.   Investigation Of Applicant: All applications for a license to conduct a
business connected with the storage, handling, sale or preparation of food or
drink intended for human consumption shall be referred to the appropriate
Village official, who shall make or cause to be made an investigation of the
premises to be used and report his findings thereon, recommending or advising
against the issuance of the license. (1990 Code § 13.307; amd. 2019 Code)
   D.   Revocation Of License: Any food dealer's license may be revoked by the
Village President for repeated violations of the provisions of this chapter or
for any violation of any other ordinance provision relating to the conduct of
the business, the condition of the premises, the article sold or the license
required. (1990 Code § 13.303)
4-2-3: UNWHOLESOME, ADULTERATED FOOD:
   A.   Unwholesome Food:
      1.   No person, firm or corporation shall offer for sale, or keep for the
purpose of selling or offering for sale, any food of any kind intended for
human consumption which is spoiled or tainted or is unwholesome and unfit for
human consumption for any reason. (1990 Code §§ 13.304, 13.401)
      2.   All tainted or unwholesome food intended for human consumption may
be condemned by the appropriate Village official and shall thereupon be seized
and destroyed by said official. (1990 Code § 13.304; amd. 2019 Code)
   B.   Adulterated Food: It shall be unlawful to sell, offer for sale, or keep
for such purpose any food or drink intended for human consumption which has
been adulterated by any material harmful in any way or which does not comply
with this Code and/or State Statutes governing the same. (1990 Code § 13.305;
amd. 2019 Code)
4-2-4: SANITARY CONDITIONS:
   A.   Premises:
      1.   Premises used for the sale or storage of food intended for human
consumption must be kept in a clean and sanitary condition.
      2.   It shall be unlawful to permit any accumulation of refuse or waste
of any kind to remain thereon for more than twenty four (24) hours, and it
shall be unlawful to permit any decaying animal or plant material to remain on
such premises. (1990 Code §§ 13.306, 13.402)
      3.   Premises used for the storage, preparation or sale of food intended
for human consumption shall be kept free from flies, vermin and rodents. (1990
Code § 13.308)
   B.   Employees:
      1.   All persons engaged in handling or coming in contact with food
intended for sale for human consumption shall keep themselves clean, both as to
person and clothing. (1990 Code § 13.309)
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person who is afflicted with or a
carrier of any infectious or contagious disease to handle or be engaged in the
care or preparation of any food or drink; and it shall be unlawful to permit
any such person to be employed in or about any premises where food or drink is
stored, prepared or sold, or to deliver any such food or drink. (1990 Code §§
13.309, 13.402)
   C.   Utensils: Utensils for personal use in all places serving food or drink
to the public shall be thoroughly cleaned and sterilized after each such usage.
(1990 Code § 13.409)
4-2-5: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter shall
be fined not less than five dollars ($5.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00) for each offense. A separate offense shall be deemed
committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (1990
Code § 13.311; amd. 2019 Code)
CHAPTER 3
GARBAGE AND REFUSE
SECTION:
4-3-1: Collection Fees
4-3-2: Receptacle Requirements
4-3-3: Prohibited Deposits; Disposal Requirements
4-3-4: Additional Prohibitions
4-3-5: Penalty
4-3-1: COLLECTION FEES:
The monthly rates of the Village residents for garbage and recycling collection
fees shall be seventeen dollars ($17.00) per unit per month, effective May 1,
2014; seventeen dollars sixty eight cents ($17.68) per unit per month,
effective May 1, 2015; eighteen dollars thirty eight cents ($18.38) per unit
per month, effective May 1, 2016; nineteen dollars eleven cents ($19.11) per
unit per month, effective May 1, 2017; and nineteen dollars eighty seven cents
($19.87) per unit per month, effective May 1, 2018, until further amended.
(Ord. 14-02, 4-7-2014)
4-3-2: RECEPTACLE REQUIREMENTS:
It shall be the duty of every owner or agent or occupant of any house,
building, flat or apartment, or tenement in the Village whose people reside,
board, or lodge, or where animal or vegetable matter is prepared or served, and
at all times to maintain in good order, the covered receptacle provided by
Kankakee/A&J Disposal, to make the contents inaccessible to dogs and other
animals and to prevent the breeding of flies and shall place and carry said
receptacles on the garbage collection day to the street or alley line
designated either by the Village Board of Trustees or by the garbage collector,
unless said person shall regularly dispose of his garbage or refuse outside the
corporate limits of the Village. All users affected by this section shall bring
out their garbage receptacle no earlier than twenty four (24) hours prior to
scheduled pick up and shall recover their garbage receptacles and have same
back on their property within twenty four (24) hours after pick up. (Ord. 15-
02, 4-20-2015)
4-3-3: PROHIBITED DEPOSITS; DISPOSAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   No garbage or any refuse of any kind shall be deposited in any street,
alley or public way, except for purposes of removal by a disposal company or
scavenger. (1990 Code §§ 13.202, 13.203; amd. 2019 Code)
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to deposit
anywhere in the Village any uncovered piles of refuse, garbage, offal or
carcasses of dead animals where such condition poses a threat to the public
health. Such refuse must be properly disposed of. Any uncovered pile of refuse
is hereby declared to be a threat to the public health. (1990 Code § 13.405;
amd. 2019 Code)
4-3-4: ADDITIONAL PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to permit or store any combustible refuse in such
a way as to create a fire hazard, or to store or throw away any refuse of any
kind in any alley, street or other public way in the Village. (1990 Code §
19.112)
   B.   Any person who violates any provision of this section is guilty of a
petty offense, and for the first offense shall be fined not to exceed one
hundred dollars ($100.00), and for a second or any subsequent offense(s) shall
be fined not to exceed seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord. 03-07, 7-7-
2003, eff. 7-7-2003; amd. 2019 Code)
4-3-5: PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, any person violating any provision
of this chapter shall be fined as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2019 Code)
CHAPTER 4
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
4-4-1: Prohibited Burning; Exceptions
4-4-2: Permitted Burning
4-4-3: Restrictions Under Certain Weather Conditions
4-4-4: Days And Hours Of Burning Vegetation
4-4-5: Special Recreational Fires
4-4-6: Fires Near Structures
4-4-7: Grass And Field Fires
4-4-8: Penalties
4-4-1: PROHIBITED BURNING; EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Pursuant to this chapter, it shall be unlawful to burn any garbage at
any time in the Village except as provided in this chapter. (Ord. 03-06, 6-2-
2003; amd. 2019 Code)
   B.   No person, firm or corporation shall burn or ignite garbage at any time
or permit to remain burning any combustible rubbish, paper, cardboard or other
substance. (Ord. 00-02, 9-18-2000, eff. 10-1-2000)
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to own a trash receptacle or barrel
for purposes of burning garbage, organic refuse and leaves on the property
thereof. If such receptacle(s) is not removed within thirty (30) days after the
effective date hereof, such receptacle shall be confiscated.
   D.   It shall be unlawful to burn leaves, grass or brush on Village property
and public roadways at any time. (Ord. 03-06, 6-2-2003)
4-4-2: PERMITTED BURNING:
   A.   Residential campfires.
   B.   Burning leaves pursuant to section
4-4-4 of this chapter.
   C.   Approved recreational wood burners.
   D.   Recreation campfires permitted on property only under the following
conditions:
      1.   The fire shall be contained in a metal container not exceeding
twenty (20) square feet in plane surface area and not elevated more than ten
inches (10") above the grade level, or on cleared earth in a pit enclosed on
the sides by masonry or rock materials and not exceeding twenty (20) square
feet in area.
      2.   All trees, fences, decks and other structures shall be at least ten
feet (10') from the fire enclosure or pit.
      3.   Any fuel used shall be confined to logs or branches that are
untreated or commercially available charcoal briquettes. No other fuels are
permissible except a starter fuel designed for that purpose.
      4.   A responsible adult of at least eighteen (18) years of age shall be
in attendance at all times that the fire is burning. When adult supervision
ceases, the fire shall be extinguished with water and the coals spread out in
the enclosure.
      5.   Campfires shall be extinguished if, in the opinion of a responding
Fire Department employee, there is danger that smoke or fire will inflict
injury upon someone or will cause damage to property.
      6.   The owner of the property upon which the fire is burning shall have
consented to such fire.
   E.   Outdoor cooking fires. Charcoal or small wood fires for cooking
purposes are permitted in containers designed for cooking over such fires.
These containers shall be placed so that they do not cause fire or smoke damage
to property or injury to any person. (Ord. 03-06, 6-2-2003)
4-4-3: RESTRICTIONS UNDER CERTAIN WEATHER CONDITIONS:
No person, firm or corporation shall burn or ignite any material otherwise
lawful when the wind or other weather conditions make such burning unsafe or
dangerous to any person or property including that of the person burning or
causing the burning the same. (Ord. 00-02, 9-18-2000, eff. 10-1-2000)
4-4-4: DAYS AND HOURS OF BURNING VEGETATION:
No person, firm or corporation shall burn or ignite leaves or tree matter
except during the hours between nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:
00) P.M. on the first and third Fridays and Saturdays of each month, except
during the month of November, at which time, burning of leaves or tree matter
is allowed each day except for Sundays and Thanksgiving Day; provided, that
such fire shall be supervised at all times by the person, firm or corporation
burning or causing the burning of any leaves or tree matter and that any leaf
fire shall be located at a sufficient distance from any other property so as to
prevent endangering any such other property, and that no such burning shall
take place on any public street or sidewalk or on any Village property. (Ord.
13-10, 12-2-2013, eff. 12-2-2013)
4-4-5: SPECIAL RECREATIONAL FIRES:
With the written permission of the Fire Chief and in accordance with the
conditions prescribed by the Fire Chief, special recreational fires shall be
permitted at special events such as high school or college pep rallies. The
Fire Chief shall have sole discretion to issue a letter of permission for such
fires based upon the potential for danger to persons or property. He or she may
prescribe such mandatory conditions as are necessary or desirable to ensure the
safety of persons and property. (Ord. 03-06, 6-2-2003)
4-4-6: FIRES NEAR STRUCTURES:
It shall be unlawful to build or light any bonfire so close to any building or
