passes through a wood or plastered partition, it shall be surrounded by a body
of brick, tile, porous terra cotta or other incombustible materials. (1990 Code
§ 14.124)
   C.   Concrete Slab Required For Unattached Buildings: Any outbuilding less
than one hundred fifty (150) square feet or less than ten feet by fifteen feet
(10' x 15') in size only requires three inches (3") of gravel base and
skirting, and any larger outbuilding constructed within the Village shall have
not less than a four inch (4") reinforced concrete slab with a rat barrier
twelve inches (12") down and twelve inches (12") beyond said slab. (Ord. 13-09,
12-2-2013, eff. 12-2-2013)
9-1-11: ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
The building inspector shall have the power and duty to enforce the provisions
of this title, and all fees provided herein shall be paid to the Village Clerk.
All permits shall be issued by the building inspector. (Ord. 03-10, 9-15-2003;
amd. 2019 Code)
9-1-12: INTERPRETATION:
Whenever in the building regulations, it is provided that anything must be done
to the approval of or subject to the direction of the building inspector or any
other officer of the Village, this shall be construed to give officer only the
discretion of determining whether there has been compliance with the rules and
standards established by ordinance, and no such provision shall be construed as
giving any officer discretionary powers as to what such regulations or
standards shall be, or power to require conditions not prescribed by ordinance,
or to enforce ordinance provisions in any arbitrary or discriminatory manner.
(Ord. 03-10, 9-15-2003)
9-1-13: PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provision of this chapter or
doing any work not authorized by this chapter shall be fined not less than
twenty five dollars ($25.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00) for each offense, and a separate offense shall be deemed committed on
each day during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (Ord. 03-10, 9-15-
2003; amd. 2019 Code)
CHAPTER 2
BUILDING OPERATIONS
SECTION:
9-2-1: Use Of Streets
9-2-2: Obstruction Or Removal Of Sidewalks
9-2-3: Safeguards
9-2-4: Prohibited Hours
9-2-1: USE OF STREETS:
The use of streets for the storage of materials in the process of construction
or alteration of a building or structure may be granted when the same will not
unduly interfere with traffic and will not reduce the usable width of the
roadway to less than eighteen feet (18'). No portion of the street, other than
that directly abutting on the premises on which work is being done, shall be
used, except with the consent of the owner or occupant of the premises abutting
on such portion. Any person seeking to make such use of the street shall file
an application for a permit therefor with the building inspector, together with
a bond with sureties to be approved by the Village Board of Trustees to
indemnify the Village for any loss or damage which may be incurred by such
occupation. (1990 Code § 14.201)
9-2-2: OBSTRUCTION OR REMOVAL OF SIDEWALKS:
No sidewalk shall be obstructed in the course of building construction or
alteration without a special permit from the building inspector, and whenever
removal of a sidewalk is required in such work, a special permit from the
building inspector shall be obtained. (1990 Code § 14.203)
9-2-3: SAFEGUARDS:
It shall be the duty of the person, firm, partnership, association or
corporation doing any construction, altering or wrecking work in the Village to
do the same with proper care for the safety of persons and property. Warnings,
barricades and lights shall be maintained whenever necessary for the protection
of pedestrians or traffic, and temporary roofs over sidewalks shall be
constructed whenever there is danger from falling articles or materials to
pedestrians. (1990 Code § 14.204)
9-2-4: PROHIBITED HOURS:
No construction or alteration operations shall be carried on between the hours
of nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. the following day if
the same are accompanied by loud noises. (1990 Code § 14.202; amd. 2019 Code)
CHAPTER 3
PLUMBING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-3-1: Compliance With Certain Regulations
9-3-2: Inspections And Tests
9-3-1: COMPLIANCE WITH CERTAIN REGULATIONS:
   A.   All plumbing shall be considered an alteration as provided in chapter 1
of this title and shall be subject to any and all rules and regulations set
forth by the building inspector. (1990 Code § 14.105)
   B.   Any building being built, converted or altered, as provided in chapter
1 of this title, shall comply with all sanitary regulations set forth by the
Village building inspector. (1990 Code § 14.126)
   C.   All water and sewer connections and all plumbing fixtures installed in
buildings shall be constructed according to the Illinois State Plumbing Code.
(1990 Code § 14.121)
9-3-2: INSPECTIONS AND TESTS:
In all buildings hereafter erected, both public and private, and in all
buildings already built or erected wherein any plumbing is installed or wherein
any sewer connected pipe shall be repaired or changed, except for minor
repairs, on the sewer side of the trap, the drain, the soil, rainwater and
other pipe or pipes connected directly or indirectly to any drain, soil or
waste pipe, and all traps, shall be exposed to view for inspection and test by
the building inspector and shall not be covered until such test is made. (1990
Code § 14.301)
CHAPTER 4
ELECTRICAL REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-4-1: Definition Of Electrical Equipment
9-4-2: Permit And Inspection Requirements
9-4-3: Installation Of Electrical Equipment
9-4-1: DEFINITION OF ELECTRICAL EQUIPMENT:
The term electrical equipment, as used in this chapter, includes, but is not
limited to, the wiring involved in the transmission of electrical current, but
expressly excludes electrical appliances and lighting switches. (1990 Code §
14.406)
9-4-2: PERMIT AND INSPECTION REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permit And Inspection Required:
      1.   From and after the effective date hereof, it shall be unlawful to
install or alter the electrical equipment or cause the same installation or
alteration to be done to a building or an area adjacent thereto within the
Village without having an electrical permit therefor from the inspector for the
Village. (1990 Code § 14.402; amd. 2019 Code)
      2.   No electrical permit shall be issued until the inspector for the
Village has been notified that installations or alterations of electrical
equipment are to be made, naming the person contemplating such work, the
proposed time of the commencement of such work, the location of such work, the
estimated cost of such work, along with the permit fee, if any, and express
written permission allowing the inspector to enter upon said location where
such work is contemplated at any time the inspector shall deem proper for the
purpose of inspecting the electrical work; provided, that any refusal of the
permission to enter upon said premises shall constitute a revocation of the
permit; provided further, that whenever it appears to any person contemplating
such work that the proposed time for commencement of any such work shall become
different than that to which the inspector has been notified, it shall be
necessary to notify the inspector of such different time at least three (3)
days prior to commencing the proposed work; provided further, that all notices
required in this subsection A2 shall be in writing, signed by the person
contemplating the work, unless the inspector shall, in his discretion, issue
the permit on oral notice. All proposed electrical installations or alterations
shall be in accordance with the general and specific standards and
specifications in section
9-4-3 of this chapter before such permit shall issue. (1990 Code § 14.403; amd.
2019 Code)
   B.   Permit Fees: The inspector for the Village shall charge no fee for the
permit for installation or alteration of electrical equipment where the total
cost of such installation or alteration is not more than five dollars ($5.00),
but shall charge the following amounts for the following total costs of
installation or alteration: (1990 Code § 14.404; amd. 2019 Code)
      1.   A fee of ten dollars ($10.00) for installation or alteration of
electrical equipment which total cost shall exceed fifty dollars ($50.00) but
not exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00).
      2.   A fee of twenty dollars ($20.00) for installation or alteration of
electrical equipment which total cost shall exceed one hundred dollars
($100.00) but not exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00).
      3.   A fee of fifty dollars ($50.00) for installation or alteration of
electrical equipment which total cost shall exceed five hundred dollars
($500.00).
      4.   A fee of eighty dollars ($80.00) for installation or alteration of
electrical equipment in commercial buildings. (1990 Code § 14.404)
   C.   Revocation Of Permit; Appeal:
      1.   The inspector for the Village is hereby empowered to revoke the
electrical permit of any person to whom such has been issued if and when such
person shall fail to make such electrical installation or alteration in
accordance with the general and specific standards and specifications in
section
9-4-3 of this chapter.
      2.   When the electrical permit has been revoked, either orally or in
writing, it shall be necessary for the person to appeal such revocation by
notifying the Village President in writing within ten (10) days of such
revocation. The appeal shall be heard before the Village Board of Trustees at
their next regularly scheduled meeting. The Board shall be empowered to take
testimony at such time and shall render a decision thereupon by a vote of yea
and nay. A majority vote of the Trustees present is required to reverse the
revocation of the inspector for the Village. Continuances on the hearing shall
be granted for good cause shown. (1990 Code § 14.405; amd. 2019 Code)
      3.   If an appeal is not taken from the revocation or the appeal, if
taken, does not reverse the revocation, this shall have the effect of rendering
the permit issued null and void from its very inception, and the person shall
remove the electrical equipment or be in violation of this chapter and subject
to the penalties hereinafter provided. (1990 Code § 14.405)
   D.   Penalty: Any person guilty of installing or altering electrical
equipment without a permit so to do shall be fined not less than five dollars
($5.00) nor more than fifty dollars ($50.00) for each offense. Each day that
said offense occurs shall be considered a separate offense. (1990 Code §
14.410)
9-4-3: INSTALLATION OF ELECTRICAL EQUIPMENT:
   A.   General Standards And Specifications: All installations or alterations
of electrical equipment in any building or buildings and/or any area adjacent
thereto and adjoining thereupon shall be made and done in accordance with the
procedures, specifications, standards and materials defined and established by
the 2014 edition of the National Electrical Code which is incorporated herein
and by reference hereto made a part hereof, except where otherwise provided
hereinafter. (1990 Code § 14.407; amd. 2019 Code)
   B.   Specific Standards And Specifications:
      1.   All wires and apparatus installed, altered or used in buildings or
parts of buildings used as a hotel, motel, lodging house, rooming house,
clubhouse, home for the aged, home for children, jail, police station,
hospital, department store, office building, school, apartment house with three
(3) or more apartments, auditorium, place of worship, commercial building,
factory, residential basement and mobile home shall be wired in standard
conduit or metal raceway wiring. (1990 Code § 14.408; amd. 2019 Code)
      2.   All residential homes shall be wired in conduit, BX, armored cable
or romex with bonding wire.
      3.   All kitchens therein shall be wired with not less than no. 12 wire.
      4.   All basements therein shall be wired in conduit wire.
      5.   No service switches, cutouts or meters shall be installed therein in
close proximity to laundry tubs, sinks, gas meters, radiators, stoves,
furnaces, plumbing fixtures or other grounded surfaces.
      6.   All washing machines, clothes dryers or deep freeze units shall have
a grounded receptacle. (1990 Code § 14.409)
CHAPTER 5
FENCES
SECTION:
9-5-1: Height In Residential Districts
9-5-2: Barbed Wire And Electric Fences
9-5-3: Definition Of A Fence
9-5-4: Fence Construction And Maintenance
9-5-5: Location And Height
9-5-1: HEIGHT IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to construct any fence on an area zoned for
residential purposes only to a height greater than eight feet (8') above the
ground level. (1990 Code § 19.122)
   B.   Any person who violates this section, upon conviction, is guilty of a
petty offense, and for the first offense shall be fined not to exceed one
hundred dollars ($100.00), and for a second or any subsequent offense(s) shall
be fined not to exceed seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord. 03-07, 7-7-
2003, eff. 7-7-2003; amd. 2019 Code)
9-5-2: BARBED WIRE AND ELECTRIC FENCES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to maintain or construct any fence composed, in
whole or part, of barbed wire or with any similar materials designed to cause
injury to persons or any wire charged with electrical current anywhere within
the Village except to protect industrial property, in which case, barbed wire
must be at least six feet (6') above the sidewalk and extend inward of the
property. (1990 Code § 10.116)
   B.   Any person who violates this section, upon conviction, is guilty of a
petty offense, and for the first offense shall be fined not to exceed one
hundred dollars ($100.00), and for a second or any subsequent offense(s) shall
be fined not to exceed seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord. 03-07, 7-7-
2003, eff. 7-7-2003; amd. 2019 Code)
9-5-3: DEFINITION OF A FENCE:
A structure made of approved materials enclosing or dividing a piece of land.
Approved materials include wood, vinyl, PVC, composite, aluminum, chain-link,
metal, or split rail. Non-approved materials for fencing include open wire,
fabric, or snow fencing. If a current fence does not conform to these
standards, then it must follow the building guidelines when replaced. (Ord. 23-
07, 11-20-2023)
9-5-4: FENCE CONSTRUCTION AND MAINTENANCE:
   A.   Property owners must first obtain a building permit from the Village
before constructing a fence. All fence posts must be securely installed below
the frost-line with a minimum depth of forty two inches (42") using a concrete
mix or expanding fence post foam.
   B.   Property owner must provide a plat of survey (original or copy) that
indicates the location, height, and type of the proposed fence including any
gates, utility equipment (such as transformers), sewer manholes, etc.
   C.   Temporary/no-dig fences are only permitted as a means to temporarily
provide a safe barrier around a construction site or area that is unsafe for
human entry. No dig fences cannot be used as a means to house or temporarily
house animals. Temporary/no-dig fences will require a permit and will come with
a restriction time of no more than thirty (30) days from time that permit was
issued. Once the thirty (30) day period has been met, the temporary fence will
need to be removed. Temporary/no-dig fences around areas such as ornamental and
vegetable gardens as a means to combat animal infiltration are permitted with a
height restriction of twenty four inches (24").
   D.   A fence shall be maintained and trimmed to the maximum height as set
forth in this chapter.
   E.   Fences shall be erected so that all supporting members shall be
attached to and located within the lot line fenced. All wooden fences shall be
constructed in such a manner that the finished side faces to the exterior of
the lot fenced.
   F.   All fences shall be constructed in conformity with wind, stress,
foundational, structural, and other requirements of the building codes and
ordinances of the Village of Chebanse.
   G.   All fences shall be maintained in a good and structurally sound manner.
When a portion of a fence suffers damage or reaches a point that renders
repair, the fence shall be replaced with the same material and style as when
first installed. Temporary patches are permitted, but will need to be replaced
with a new section of fence within thirty (30) days of initial cause of damage.
If fence is in disrepair, the fence must be brought up to standards or owner
may face a fine of no less than seventy five dollars ($75.00) and no more than
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00).
   H.   All fences shall be of one color of wood, paint or stain, whether
solid, transparent or translucent, in a natural tone or color. Advertising,
murals, artwork and/or odd or disparate colors of such are not permitted in
residential areas or zones on the exterior faced side of any such fence.
   I.   Business or Industrial areas or zones must receive written Village
Board approval prior to applying any advertising or artwork to the fences. The
Village may require descriptive renderings prior to such approval. Temporary
advertising for help or postings to fill a employment position are allowed and
exempt from such requirements.
   J.   No gate across driveway in the front or side yard. Gate shall not swing
over public walk.
   K.   Post shall not extend beyond six inches (6") above the height of the
fence. Bottom edge of the fence to be installed no more than two inches (2")
above grade. Call J.U.L.I.E. at 1-800-892-0123 before you dig.
   L.   Chain link shall have no slats and top edge shall be folded down to
have a knuckle edge. Provide a minimum twenty-four-inch (24") clearance and
access to utility equipment on the property within easements.
   M.   Fences are not allowed on vacant properties.
   N.   Any fence found to be in violation may be declared a nuisance. (Ord.
23-07, 11-20-2023)
9-5-5: LOCATION AND HEIGHT:
   A.   Fences in areas that are zoned as commercial may be installed directly
on the property line.
   B.   Residential fences may be constructed on or inside the lot line and
shall not be closer than two feet (2') to any public right-of-way.
   C.   No private fences shall be constructed on a public street or alley.
   D.   Fences may be placed on public utility easements so long as the
structures do not interfere in any way with the existing underground, ground,
or above ground utilities. The owner shall assume the responsibility to notify
all utility companies of the intent to erect a fence upon a public utility
right of way. The Village or any utility that has authority to use such
easements shall not be liable for repair or replacement of such fences in the
event they are moved, damaged, or destroyed due to the lawful use of the
easement.
   E.   If a non-conforming fence is in disrepair or needs replaced, it must be
replaced or repaired to conforming standards herein.
   F.   Fences must be four feet (4') from the front of the house to the front
property line and must stay twelve inches (12") off the front property line.
   G.   Definitions:
 
                            For a determination of fence locations for a corner
                            lot, the street address will determine the front of
                            the home. A fence may continue into the side yard
                            of the corner lot a maximum ten feet (10') from the
                            home with a maximum height of six feet (6'). Any
                            fence located farther than ten feet (10') from the
CORNER LOT SIDE YARDS:      home into the side yard of the corner lot may be
                            installed at a four foot (4') maximum height
                            provided it is at least fifty percent (50%) open.
                            No chain-link fences will be allowed in the side
                            yard of a corner lot. No fence may be located
                            within five feet (5') of any sidewalk or located
                            closer than seventeen feet (17') from the edge of a
                            curb line, whichever is more restrictive.
                            In front yards, the maximum height shall be forty-
FRONT YARDS:                eight inches (48"). However, no fence shall exceed
