10-11-3: PARKING CERTAIN VEHICLES AND ITEMS IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS:
   A.   All equipment or tools or junk motor vehicles shall be parked or stored
in a completely enclosed structure on any residential premises except when
making a delivery or rendering a service at such premises.
   B.   All equipment or tools which are not used in the regular operation of a
business or appear to be discarded, or junk vehicles of any kind, shall be
parked or stored in a completely enclosed structure on any residential
premises. This shall also include equipment, materials or tools which
reasonably appear to be not in use. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-11-4: DRIVEWAYS:
All driveways installed, altered, changed, replaced, or extended after the
effective date hereof shall meet the following requirements:
   A.   Openings for vehicular ingress and egress shall not exceed twenty four
feet (24') at the street line and thirty feet (30') at the roadway.
   B.   Vehicular entrances and exits to drive-in theaters, banks, and
restaurants; motels; funeral homes; vehicular sales, service, washing, and
repair stations; garages; or public parking lots shall not be less than two
hundred feet (200') from any pedestrian entrance or exit to a school, college,
university, church, hospital, park, playground, library, public emergency
shelter, or other place of public assembly. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-11-5: ACCESS TO RIGHTS-OF-WAY:
   A.   No direct private access shall be permitted to the existing or proposed
rights-of-way of expressways nor to any controlled access arterial street
without permission of the highway agency that has control jurisdiction and of
the Planning Commission and the Village Board of Trustees.
   B.   No direct public or private access shall be permitted to the existing
or proposed rights-of-way of the following:
      1.   Freeways, interstate highways, and their interchanges or turning
lanes, nor to intersecting or interchanging streets within one thousand five
hundred feet (1,500') of the most remote end of the taper of the turning lanes.
      2.   Arterial streets intersecting another arterial street within one
hundred feet (100') of the intersection of the right-of-way lines.
      3.   Streets intersecting an arterial street within fifty feet (50') of
the intersection of the right-of-way lines.
      4.   Access barriers such as curbing, fencing, ditching, landscaping, or
other topographic barriers shall be erected to prevent unauthorized vehicular
ingress or egress to the above specified streets or highways.
      5.   Temporary access to the above rights-of-way may be granted by the
Village Planning Commission after review and recommendation by the highway
agencies having jurisdiction. Such access permit shall be temporary, revocable,
and subject to any condition required, and shall be issued for a period not to
exceed twelve (12) months. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
CHAPTER 12
SIGNS
SECTION:
10-12-1: Purpose
10-12-2: Permit And Fee Requirements
10-12-3: Directional And Informational Signs
10-12-4: Obstructions By Signs Prohibited
10-12-5: Maintenance; Repair Or Removal
10-12-6: Unsafe, Unlawful Signs
10-12-7: Nonconforming Signs
10-12-8: Permitted Signs In Zoning Districts
10-12-8-1: Residential Districts
10-12-8-2: Business Districts
10-12-8-3: Industrial Districts
10-12-9: Exemptions From Provisions
10-12-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to provide a guide to the location, size,
content and placement of signs throughout the Village so that signs are both
effective and compatible with the environment. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-2: PERMIT AND FEE REQUIREMENTS:
The permit and fee requirements shall be as indicated in the applicable
building permit fee schedule. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-3: DIRECTIONAL AND INFORMATIONAL SIGNS:
   A.   Permitted In Any District: Directional or informational signs of a
public or semipublic nature, not exceeding eight (8) square feet in area, are
permitted in any district. Such signs may not be illuminated but may be of the
beaded reflector or phosphorescent type. Such signs shall be of the types and
contain only such displays as follows:
      1.   Permanent signs displaying the name and location of the Village,
airport, hospital, community center, private school, college, YMCA, YWCA,
church or other place of worship; or the name or place of meeting of an
official or civic body such as the Chamber of Commerce, Rotary, Kiwanis, or
other similar service or community clubs.
      2.   Temporary signs displaying the name, location, and time of an event
of public interest such as a State or County Fair, public or general election,
circus, rodeo, or other such event in connection with which the support of the
general public is essential to the success of the event. Such sign shall be
removed within ten (10) days after the event is over.
   B.   State Highway Directional Signs: State highway directional signs and
markings and signs announcing the location of or directing traffic to given
locations shall be made and installed in accordance with the specifications of
the State Highway Department and require a State permit. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-4: OBSTRUCTIONS BY SIGNS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Obstruction Of Entrances: A sign erected in any district shall not be
constructed and/or maintained so as to obstruct any fire escape, window, door
or opening used as a means of entrance or egress for firefighting purposes, or
so as to prevent free passage from one part of a roof to any other part thereof
or to another roof. No sign shall be attached in any form, shape or manner to a
fire escape or be so placed as to interfere with any opening required for legal
ventilation.
   B.   Obstruction Of View: No sign of any kind shall be located or placed so
as to interfere with the full view of vehicular traffic in all directions.
(Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-5: MAINTENANCE; REPAIR OR REMOVAL:
The Code Enforcement Officer is hereby authorized to determine whether or not a
sign is adequately maintained and shall order repaired or removed any sign
which is not being adequately maintained. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-6: UNSAFE, UNLAWFUL SIGNS:
   A.   Notice To Remove Or Alter: If the Code Enforcement Officer finds that
any sign is unsafe or insecure, or is a menace to the public, or has been
constructed or erected or is being maintained in violation of the provisions of
this chapter, he/she shall give written notice to the person to whom the
certificate has been issued.
   B.   Removal Or Alteration By Village; Costs: If the person to whom the
certificate has been issued fails to remove or alter the sign to comply with
the standards herein set forth within ten (10) days after sign notice, such
sign may be removed or altered by the Code Enforcement Officer in a manner that
will comply. Such action shall be at the expense of the property owner upon
whose land the sign is located.
   C.   Summary Removal: The Code Enforcement Officer may cause any sign which
is an immediate peril to the persons or property to be summarily removed. (Ord.
02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-7: NONCONFORMING SIGNS:
A sign lawfully established before the effective date hereof but not conforming
with the regulations hereof may remain. Minor repairs and maintenance of such
signs and the repainting and change of display of an existing painted bulletin
sign and changing display of an existing poster panel sign is not affected by
this title. Replacements or enlargements are not permitted. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-
2002)
10-12-8: PERMITTED SIGNS IN ZONING DISTRICTS:
10-12-8-1: RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS:
   A.   Nameplates And Identification Signs (Nonflashing And Nonilluminated):
      1.   Size: Not more than two (2) square feet in area.
      2.   Height: Said sign shall be located on the principal structure.
      3.   Setbacks: Said sign shall be located on the principal structure.
      4.   Number: One nameplate for each principal farm dwelling. On a corner
lot, two (2) such nameplates for each dwelling unit, one facing each street.
      5.   Contents: The name of the occupant, name and address of the building
on the lot, or permitted home occupation.
   B.   "For Sale" And "To Rent" Signs (Nonflashing And Nonilluminated):
      1.   Size: No sign shall exceed twelve (12) square feet in area.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than fifteen feet (15') above
average grade.
      3.   Setbacks: No nearer than ten feet (10') from a right-of- way line
adjoining a street; no nearer than five feet (5') from an interior side or rear
lot line.
      4.   Number: No more than one such sign per lot; except, that on a corner
lot, two (2) signs, one facing each street, shall be permitted.
      5.   Contents: Name, address, and phone number of seller or agent.
   C.   Church Bulletin Signs (Nonflashing And Nonilluminated):
      1.   Size: No sign shall exceed sixteen (16) square feet in area.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than fifteen feet (15') above
average grade.
      3.   Setback: No sign shall be nearer than ten feet (10') from the right-
of-way adjoining a street.
      4.   Number: There shall be not more than one sign per lot; except, that
on a corner lot, two (2) signs, one facing each street, shall be permitted.
(Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-8-2: BUSINESS DISTRICTS:
   A.   General Requirements:
      1.   Sign Supports:
         a.   Sign display surfaces not attached to a building or awning shall
be supported by not more than two (2) columns, each having a diameter of not
more than six inches (6") or, in the case of a single column, not less than
eight inches (8").
         b.   Signs on awnings shall be exempt from the limitations imposed by
this chapter; provided, that any sign located on an awning shall be affixed
flat to the surface thereof, shall be nonilluminated, and shall indicate only
the name or address of the establishment in the building to which it is
attached. No such sign shall extend vertically or horizontally beyond the
limits of said awning.
      2.   Illumination And Movement:
         a.   Signs may have constant or flashing illumination.
         b.   No sign display shall have or consist of moving parts.
         c.   A sign located in direct line of vision of any traffic control
sign shall not have flashing or intermittent illumination of red, green, or
amber color.
         d.   Where a sign is illuminated by light reflected upon it, light
rays shall not beam directly upon any part of any residential building nor into
a Residential District or street.
   B.   Business Signs:
      1.   Size: The gross surface area in square feet of all signs on a lot
shall not exceed one times the linear feet of street frontage of such lot. On
corner lots or through lots, each lot line abutting a street shall be
considered a separate frontage. On a corner lot, only the lot line having the
narrowest width abutting a street shall be considered in calculating frontage.
This includes border and trim, but it excludes ornamental base or apron,
supports and other structural members. The maximum size limitation shall apply
to each side of a sign or sign structure.
      2.   Setback: A business not attached to a building shall be located not
less than twenty feet (20') from a right-of-way line abutting a street or five
feet (5') from a rear or interior side lot line.
      3.   Height:
         a.   A sign attached to a building wall shall project not more than
six feet (6') above the building height or thirty feet (30') above the ground,
whichever is lower. A sign projecting from a building wall more than eight
inches (8") shall have its lowest level not less than seven feet (7') above the
grade of the ground directly below it.
         b.   A sign not attached to a building wall shall project not more
than thirty feet (30') above average grade of the ground at the sign structure.
         c.   Any sign not attached to a building wall and which is located
nearer than fifty feet (50') from the intersection of two (2) or more streets
shall have the bottom of the display surface not less than twelve feet (12')
above either the grade of the ground or the pavement below it.
      4.   Number: Only one sign which is either affixed to or painted on a
building wall or a freestanding ground sign shall be permitted on any lot in
this district having eighty feet (80') or less of frontage on a street. On a
lot having more than eighty feet (80') of frontage, one additional sign shall
be permitted for each eighty feet (80') of additional frontage.
   C.   Advertising Signs:
      1.   For purposes of this section, an advertising sign is defined as a
sign containing information directing attention to a business, commodity,
service or entertainment conducted, sold or offered at a location other than
the premises on which the sign is located.
      2.   Advertising signs may be permitted only where allowed as a permitted
use in the zoning district in which it is located. (Ord. 16-03, 6-6-2016)
   D.   Unified Shopping Center Signs:
      1.   Size: The square footage of any sign shall not exceed twice the
linear feet of frontage of such lot.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than thirty feet (30') above
the grade of the ground below it.
      3.   Setback: Such sign shall be set back a minimum of fifteen feet (15')
from the right-of-way on a lot line adjoining a street.
      4.   Number: One sign on each street frontage in addition to those
described above.
      5.   Contents: Such sign shall advertise only the name and location of
the center or individual use and the name and type of business of each occupant
of the center.
   E.   Nameplates And Identification Signs (Nonflashing And Nonilluminated):
      1.   Size: Not more than six (6) square feet in area.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than fifteen feet (15') above
average grade.
      3.   Setback: No nearer than ten feet (10') from a right-of-way line
adjoining a street; no nearer than five feet (5') from an interior side or rear
lot line.
      4.   Number: One nameplate for each principal farm dwelling; on a corner
lot, two (2) such nameplates for each dwelling unit, one facing each street and
such additional signs as required for crop identification during the growing
season.
      5.   Contents: The name of the occupant, name and address of the building
on the lot, and specialized agricultural activity.
   F.   "For Sale" And "To Rent" Signs (Nonflashing And Nonilluminated):
      1.   Size: No sign shall exceed thirty (30) square feet in area.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than fifteen feet (15') above
average grade.
      3.   Setback: No nearer than ten feet (10') from a right-of-way line
adjoining a street; no nearer than five feet (5') from an interior side or rear
lot line.
      4.   Number: No more than one such sign per lot; except, that on a corner
lot, two (2) signs, one facing each street, shall be permitted.
      5.   Contents: Name, address, and phone number of agent. (Ord. 02-04, 6-
3-2002)
10-12-8-3: INDUSTRIAL DISTRICTS:
   A.   Business Signs: Business signs as regulated within this section
10-12-8.
   B.   Industrial Parks Or Planned Unit Developments:
      1.   Size: The square footage of any sign shall not exceed twice the
linear feet of frontage of such lot.
      2.   Height: No sign shall project higher than thirty feet (30') above
average grade.
      3.   Setback: Such a sign shall be set back a minimum of twenty feet
(20') from the front lot line of such industrial park or planned development.
      4.   Number: One additional sign on each street frontage, other than
those regulated above.
      5.   Contents: Such sign shall advertise only the name and location of
the industrial park or planned unit development and the name and type of
business of each occupant of the park.
   C.   Nameplate And Identification Signs: Nameplate and identification signs
as regulated within the Business Districts.
   D.   For Sale And To Rent Signs: For sale and to rent signs as regulated
within the Business Districts. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-2002)
10-12-9: EXEMPTIONS FROM PROVISIONS:
The following signs are exempt from the provisions of this chapter:
   A.   Memorial signs displayed on private property not exceeding six (6)
square feet in area.
   B.   Governmental flags and insignia, when not used for commercial purposes.
   C.   Legal notices.
   D.   Governmental traffic, parking, and directional signs. (Ord. 02-04, 6-3-
2002)
CHAPTER 13
NONCONFORMITIES
SECTION:
10-13-1: Zoning Permit; Certificate Of Occupancy
10-13-2: Nonconforming Structures
10-13-3: Nonconforming Uses
10-13-4: Additional Requirements For Nonconforming Structures And Uses
10-13-5: Substandard Lots
10-13-6: Variances
10-13-1: ZONING PERMIT; CERTIFICATE OF OCCUPANCY:
A zoning permit shall be required for all lawful nonconforming uses of land and
buildings created by the adoption of this title, or a certificate of occupancy
may be authorized by the Village Board of Trustees for the Code Enforcement
Officer to require that nonconforming uses maintain valid certificates of
occupancy identifying them as nonconforming uses, as applicable. (Ord., 5-7-
1973)
10-13-2: NONCONFORMING STRUCTURES:
   A.   Maintenance: A nonconforming structure lawfully existing upon the
effective date hereof may be maintained, except as otherwise provided in this
section.
   B.   Repairs: A nonconforming structure may be repaired or altered provided
no structural change shall be made.
   C.   Additions, Enlargements Or Moving:
      1.   A structure nonconforming as to use, height, yard requirements or
lot area shall not be added to or enlarged in any manner unless such structure,
including such addition or enlargement, is made to conform to the use, height,
yard, and area requirements of the district in which it is located.
      2.   No nonconforming structure shall be moved, in whole or in part, to
any other location on the lot on which it is located unless every portion of
such structure is made to conform to all the requirements of the district in
which it is located. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-13-3: NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   Continuation And Change Of Use: Except as otherwise provided in this
title:
      1.   A nonconforming use lawfully existing upon the effective date hereof
may be continued.
      2.   A nonconforming use may be changed only to a use of the same or more
restricted classification.
   B.   Expansion Of Use Prohibited:
      1.   A nonconforming use in a structure designed for a conforming use
shall not be expanded or extended into any other portion of such conforming
structure nor changed except to a conforming use.
      2.   A nonconforming use on a part of a lot shall not be expanded or
extended into any other portion of such lot. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-13-4: ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS FOR NONCONFORMING STRUCTURES AND USES:
   A.   Discontinuance Of Use: Whenever a nonconforming use has been
discontinued for a period of twelve (12) months, such use shall not thereafter
be reestablished, and the use thereafter shall conform to the provisions of
this title.
   B.   Damaged Structures: No building damaged by fire or other causes to the
extent that its restoration will cost more than sixty percent (60%) of its fair
cash value shall be repaired or rebuilt except to conform to the provisions of
this title.
   C.   Unattached Nonconforming Billboards Or Signs: Any nonconforming
billboard or advertising structure not attached to a building lawfully existing
upon the effective date hereof shall be discontinued on or before ten (10)
years after the effective date hereof unless a discontinuance date has been
established by a prior zoning ordinance, in which case, such prior date of
discontinuance shall apply. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-13-5: SUBSTANDARD LOTS:
In any Residential District, a one-family detached dwelling and its accessory
structures may be erected on any legal lot or parcel of record which was
recorded in the Office of the County Recorder of Deeds before the effective
date hereof or amendment hereto. Such lot or parcel must have been in separate
ownership from abutting lands on the said effective date hereof or amendment
hereto. If abutting lands and the substandard lot are owned on that date by the
same owner, the substandard lot shall not be sold or used without full
compliance with the provisions of this title. If in separate ownership, there
shall be compliance with all the district requirements insofar as practical.
The Board of Zoning Appeals shall interpret the requirements to be followed in
such cases upon request of the Code Enforcement Officer. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-13-6: VARIANCES:
The Board of Zoning Appeals may authorize, upon appeals in specific cases, such
variance from the terms of this chapter as will not be contrary to the public
interest where, owing to special conditions, a literal enforcement of the
provisions of this chapter will result in unnecessary hardship, and so that the
spirit of this chapter shall be observed and substantial justice done;
provided, however, that no action shall be taken or decision made except after
a public hearing. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
CHAPTER 14
CONDITIONAL USES
SECTION:
10-14-1: Introduction; Use Categories
10-14-2: Planned Developments
10-14-3: Conditional Uses
10-14-1: INTRODUCTION; USE CATEGORIES:
Conditional uses, as defined in section
10-2-2 of this title, are those which cannot be adequately controlled by simple
preregulations through rigid dimensional and use standards. Conditional uses
are those which require individual review by the Planning Commission and
Village Board of Trustees to ensure conformance with the intent of all
comprehensive plan elements. Conditional uses include the following basic
categories:
   A.   Planned Development Projects: Complex projects designed to take maximum
advantage of unique site characteristics and potentials along with original
design and use concepts and submitted for review under the planned development
procedure.
   B.   Conditional Uses: Single uses or single aspects of permitted uses
specifically identified in this title as requiring individual review under the
conditional use procedure. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-14-2: PLANNED DEVELOPMENTS:
   A.   Intent: The planned development procedure is intended to provide a
single uniform procedure for total review of a proposed development, both
design and use. The procedure combines the design review procedure of
subdivision approval and the use review procedure of zoning amendments, and
enables the Planning Commission to review all aspects of a proposed development
simultaneously to permit greater flexibility and originality in concept
according to the intent of comprehensive plan elements and still to exercise
greater final control over the approved development than is possible through
preregulated zoning districts.
   B.   Standards:
      1.   Design Standards: Because the design standards for use, dimensions,
density, and qualitative attributes are subject to evolution through continuous
plan review, they are not included as an integral part of the unchanging
planned development procedure. This title refers to the officially adopted
policies, detailed area plans, and all other elements of the evolving
comprehensive plan for the standards to guide the approval of planned
development projects. A planned development project may depart from conformance
with the dimension, area, and use regulations for the standard zoning
districts, and from conformance with the design standards in the Village
subdivision regulations. However, a planned development project shall conform
with all applicable elements of the officially adopted comprehensive plan.
      2.   Required Improvements: Planned development projects shall be subject
to the regulations governing required improvements found in the Village
subdivision regulations.
      3.   Traffic, Parking, Loading And Access: Planned development projects
shall be subject to the regulations for traffic, parking, loading, and access
of this title.
      4.   Special Conditions: The Planning Commission may attach special
conditions to approval of the final plats to ensure conformance with the intent
of all official plan elements.
   C.   Procedure:
      1.   General Requirements:
         a.   A planned development project may be permitted only by amendment
to the Zoning Map according to the amendment procedure of section
10-3-6 of this title.
         b.   The Village subdivision regulations shall be followed in its
entirety whether the development shall be in single or divided ownership.
      2.   Preliminary Plat: A preliminary plat of the planned development
project shall be submitted as required by the Village subdivision regulations.
It is recommended that this submission be preceded by preapplication
conferences, as recommended by said subdivision regulations to determine
whether the developer's intent agrees with the intent expressed by all
comprehensive plan elements. Additional supporting material beyond that
required by the Village subdivision regulations for the preliminary plat shall
include:
         a.   Explanation of the character of the planned development and the
manner in which it has been planned to take advantage of the flexibility of
these regulations.
         b.   Statement of present and proposed ownership of all land within
the project.
         c.   Development schedule indicating:
            (1)   Stages in which project will be built with emphasis on area,
density, use and public facilities such as open space to be developed with each
stage. Overall design of each stage shall be shown on the plat and through
supporting graphic material.
            (2)   Approximate dates for beginning and completion of each stage.
            (3)   Agreements, provisions or covenants which will govern the
use, maintenance, and continued protection of the planned development and any
of its common open space.
      3.   Amendment Procedure: The amendment procedure established in section
10-3-6 of this title shall be initiated after conditional approval of the
preliminary plat by the Planning Commission. Under this procedure, the Zoning
Map may be amended to designate the location proposed in the preliminary plat
as a Planned Development District superseding the original zoning district. The
amendment shall be in conformance with all comprehensive plan elements. The
Planned Development District shall be valid only for that preliminary plat and
supporting material upon which the amendment was based. All supporting material
shall remain on file with the preliminary plat.
      4.   Final Plats:
         a.   If the amendment is approved, final plats shall be prepared for
each stage according to the development schedule. The final plat and supporting
material shall show in detail and design and use of all the buildings and
overall land development plans, as well as such other information the Planning
Commission may require for the complete consideration of the project, in
addition to information required by the Village subdivision regulations.
         b.   The final plat shall conform to the preliminary plat and
supporting material; except, that the Planning Commission may approve minor
changes without public hearing at this time which do not change the concept or
intent of the development.
         c.   Major changes, which are changes in density, height of buildings,
reduction of proposed open space, changes in the financing, development
schedule, or final governing agreements, provisions, or covenants, or
resubdivision, may be approved only by submission of a new preliminary plat or
applicable supporting material followed by the amendment procedure.
      5.   Continuing Control:
         a.   The planned development project shall be developed only according
to the approved and recorded final plat and all supporting material. The
recorded final plat and supporting material, together with all recorded
amendments, shall be binding on the applicants, their successors, and assigns
and shall limit and control the uses of premises and the location of structures
in the planned development project.
         b.   Minor changes in the final plat during or after construction
shall be accompanied by submission of a new preliminary plat followed by the
amendment procedure.
         c.   The Planning Commission shall consider the planned development
amendment, subject to revocations, if construction falls more than one year
behind schedule.
      6.   Fees And Permits:
         a.   The Village may establish a schedule of reasonable fees to be
charged for plat review.
         b.   Zoning permits shall be required for each structure according to
section
10-3-2 of this title. The Code Enforcement Officer shall base issuance upon
conformance with the final plat and supporting material. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-14-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
   A.   Procedure: In applying for conditional use approval, the applicant
shall follow all procedures set forth in section
10-3-2 of this title on zoning permits. The Code Enforcement Officer shall
refer the application to the Planning Commission, and the Planning Commission
shall hold a public hearing on the application. The Planning Commission may
approve, modify, or disapprove the application. In the case of approval or
approval with modification, the Planning Commission shall issue written
authorization to the Code Enforcement Officer to issue a zoning permit in full
conformance with section
10-3-2 of this title. This authorization shall remain on permanent file with
the application. The Planning Commission may attach special conditions to
ensure conformance with the intent of all comprehensive plan elements. The
commission may establish a schedule of reasonable fees to be charged for
conditional use approval.
   B.   Conditional Uses In All Districts: The following are designated as
conditional uses which may be approved in all zoning districts: public utility
and service uses such as electric substations, gas regulator stations,
telephone transmission; structure, radio, television, and microwave relay
towers; water reservoirs or pumping stations; sanitary landfills; government
buildings; transportation facilities; and similar uses.
   C.   Conditional Uses In Specified Districts: Other conditional uses may be
approved in only those zoning districts where they are designated as
conditional uses under the zoning district regulations. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
CHAPTER 15
PERFORMANCE STANDARDS
SECTION:
10-15-1: Special Regulations In Manufacturing Districts
10-15-2: Smoke And Particulate Matter
10-15-3: Toxic Matter In The M-1 And M-2 Districts
10-15-4: Odorous Matter
10-15-5: Fire And Explosive Hazards
10-15-1: SPECIAL REGULATIONS IN MANUFACTURING DISTRICTS:
   A.   Prohibited Uses In All Manufacturing Districts: The following uses are
prohibited in all Manufacturing Districts whether or not they meet the
performance standards:
Crematories.
Dumping, reduction or other processing of garbage, dead animals, offal or
refuse, except as customarily incidental to a permitted principal use.
Fireworks or explosive manufacture or storage.
Junk shops, junkyards or automobile wrecking yards.
Stockyards or slaughter of animals or fowl.
Tanning, curing, or storage of rawhides or skins.
   B.   Restrictions Regarding Explosives:
      1.   No activities involving the storage, utilization, or manufacture of
materials or products which decompose of detonation shall be permitted; except,
that these activities customarily incidental to the operation of permitted
principal use may be permitted by a variation by the Board of Zoning Appeals.
Such materials shall be stored, utilized and manufactured in accordance with
the applicable rules and regulations of the Village and the State of Illinois.
      2.   Such materials shall include, but shall not be confined to:
All high explosives such as TNT, RDX, HMX, PETN, and picric acid, propellants
and components thereof such as dry nitrocellulose, black powder, baron
hydrides, hydrazine, and its derivatives.
All primary explosives such as lead azide, lead styphnate, fulminates, and
tetracenes.
Blasting explosives such as dynamite and nitroglycerine.
Nuclear fuels, fissionable materials and products, and reactor elements such as
uranium 235 and plutonium 239.
Pyrotechnics and fireworks such as magnesium powder, potassium chlorate, and
potassium nitrate.
Strong oxidizing agents such as liquid oxygen, perchloric acid, perchlorates,
chlorates, and hydrogen peroxide in concentrations greater than thirty five
percent (35%).
Unstable organic compounds such as acetylides, tetrazoles, and ozonides.
   C.   M-1 Industrial District: The following regulations apply in the M-
1 Industrial District:
      1.   All processing shall be conducted within completely enclosed
buildings.
      2.   Storage of materials, products and goods is permitted within
completely enclosed buildings or outdoors if screened completely from public
view or not detrimental to the aesthetic condition of the area.
      3.   Outdoor storage of uncontained bulk materials is prohibited.
   D.   M-2 Industrial District: The following regulations apply in the M-
2 Industrial District:
      1.   Processing and storage of materials, products, and goods is
permitted within completely enclosed buildings or outdoors if screened properly
from public view.
      2.   Outdoor storage of uncontained bulk materials is prohibited within
twenty feet (20') of property lines.
   E.   Compliance With Provisions: Any use established in a Manufacturing
District shall be operated in such a manner as to comply with the applicable
performance standards as hereinafter set forth governing noise, vibration,
smoke, toxic matter, odors, fire and explosive hazards, and glare. No use
already established on the effective date hereof shall be so altered or
modified as to conflict with or further conflict with the applicable
performance standards for the district in which such use is located. (Ord., 5-
7-1973)
10-15-2: SMOKE AND PARTICULATE MATTER:
   A.   General Regulations:
      1.   The emission of smoke or particulate matter in such manner or
quantity as to endanger or be detrimental to the public health, safety,
comfort, or welfare is hereby declared to be a public nuisance and shall not be
permitted in any Manufacturing District.
      2.   For the purpose of grading the density or equivalent opacity of
smoke, the Ringelmann Chart described in the U.S. Bureau of Mines Information
Circular 6888 shall be employed. The emission of smoke or particulate matter of
a density or equivalent opacity greater than no. 1 on the Ringelmann Chart is
prohibited at all times except as otherwise provided hereinafter.
      3.   Dust and other types of air pollution borne by the wind from such
sources as storage areas, yards, roads, and the like, within lot boundaries,
shall be kept to a minimum by appropriate landscaping, paving, oiling, fencing,
wetting, or other acceptable means.
      4.   The open burning of refuse, paint, oil, debris, and any other
combustible material is prohibited in all Industrial Districts.
      5.   No operation shall result in the emission into the open air from any
process or control equipment, or in the measurement at any convenient measuring
point in a breeching or stack of particulate matter in the gases that exceeds
0.60 pound per thousand pounds of gases during any one hour.
      6.   Particulate matter loadings in pounds per acre described below shall
be determined by selecting a continuous four-hour period which will result in
the highest average emission rate.
   B.   M-1 Industrial District: The following regulations apply in the M-
1 Industrial District:
      1.   The emission of smoke having a density or equivalent opacity in
excess of Ringelmann no. 1 is prohibited. However, for two (2) minutes in any
four-hour period, smoke up to and including Ringelmann no. 2 shall be
permitted.
      2.   The rate of emission of particulate matter from all vents and stacks
within the boundaries of any lot shall not exceed 0.2 pound per acre of lot
area during any one hour.
   C.   M-2 Industrial District: The following regulations apply in the M-
2 Industrial District:
      1.   The emission of smoke having a density or equivalent opacity in
excess of Ringelmann no. 2 is prohibited. However, for two (2) minutes in any
four-hour period, smoke up to and including Ringelmann no. 3 shall be
permitted.
      2.   The rate of emission of particulate matter from all stacks and vents
within the boundaries of any lot shall not exceed one pound per acre of lot
area during any one hour. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-15-3: TOXIC MATTER IN THE M-1 AND M-2 DISTRICTS:
The following regulations apply in the M-1 and M-2 Industrial Districts:
   A.   The release of airborne toxic matter (including radioactive matter)
shall not exceed one-thirtieth (1/30) of the maximum permissible concentration
allowed an industrial worker when measured at any point beyond the lot line,
either at ground level or habitable elevation, whichever is more restrictive.
Concentrations shall be measured and calculated as the highest average that
will occur over a continuous twenty four-hour period.
   B.   If a toxic substance is not contained in the most recent listing of
threshold limit values published by the American Conference of Governmental
Industrial Hygienists, the applicant shall satisfy the local County Health
Department that the proposed levels will be safe to the general population.
(Ord., 5-7-1973)
10-15-4: ODOROUS MATTER:
   A.   General Regulations: The release of materials capable of becoming
odorous, either by bacterial decomposition or chemical reaction, shall meet the
standards of the district in which the odor is created.
   B.   M-1 Industrial District: When odorous matter is released from any
operation, activity, or use in the M-1 Industrial District, the concentration
of such odorous materials shall not exceed the odor threshold when measured
beyond the lot line, either at ground level or habitable elevation. (Ord., 5-7-
1973)
10-15-5: FIRE AND EXPLOSIVE HAZARDS:
   A.   In all Manufacturing Districts, the storage, utilization, or
manufacture of solid materials or products ranging from incombustible to
moderate burning is permitted.
   B.   The storage, utilization, or manufacture of solid materials or products
ranging from free or active burning to intense burning is permitted, provided
either of the following conditions is met:
      1.   Said materials or products shall be stored, utilized, or
manufactured within completely enclosed buildings having incombustible exterior
walls and protected with an automatic fire extinguishing system.
      2.   Said material, if stored outdoors, will be no less than fifty feet
(50') to the nearest lot line. (Ord., 5-7-1973)
CHAPTER 16
APPENDICES
SECTION:
10-16-1: Appendix A, Yards
