TITLE 11
SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL SUBDIVISION PROVISIONS
SECTION:
11-1-1: Purpose And Jurisdiction
11-1-2: Platting And Compliance Required
11-1-3: Acceptance Of Public Ways, Lands And Uses
11-1-4: Liability For Costs
11-1-5: Approvals, Interpretations And Exceptions
11-1-6: Violations; Penalties
11-1-1: PURPOSE AND JURISDICTION:
For the purpose and development of the Village and for the promotion of the
public health and safety, comfort, morals and welfare of the persons living
within the area governed by the Village, the provisions and regulations herein
contained shall apply to and govern the subdivision and platting of lands lying
within the corporate limits of the Village and shall also govern the
subdivision and platting of lands lying within contiguous territory not more
than one and one-half (11/2) miles beyond the corporate limits of the Village.
(Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-1-2: PLATTING AND COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
Whenever any subdivision of land shall hereafter be laid out within the
incorporated limits of the Village or within the surrounding territory not more
than one and one-half (11/2) miles beyond the incorporated boundary of the
Village, the subdivider thereof or his agent shall submit both a preliminary
and a final subdivision plan to the Village. Said plans, proposed improvements,
and all procedures relating thereto shall in all respects be in full compliance
with the regulations contained in this title. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-1-3: ACCEPTANCE OF PUBLIC WAYS, LANDS AND USES:
All lands offered to the Village for use as streets, highways, alleys, parks
and other public use shall be referred to the Village Board of Trustees for
review and acceptance. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-1-4: LIABILITY FOR COSTS:
It shall be understood that the developer and concerned utility companies shall
assume all costs for the planning and development of any and all subdivisions.
The Village shall not participate in any costs. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-1-5: APPROVALS, INTERPRETATIONS AND EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   No land shall, after the effective date hereof, be subdivided or filed
for record, nor any street laid out, nor any improvements made to the land,
until the plan or plans of the subdivision or street improvements shall have
been duly considered and approved by action of the Village Board of Trustees.
This approval must be in writing and placed on the original tracing of the
final plans, according to the procedure outlined in chapter 4 of this title.
   B.   No lot, tract or parcel of land within any subdivision shall be offered
for sale nor shall any sale, contract for sale, or option be made or given
until such subdivision plans have been properly reviewed and officially
approved by the Village Board of Trustees.
   C.   No improvements, such as sidewalks, water supply, stormwater drainage,
sewage facilities, gas service, electric service, lighting, grading, paving or
surfacing of streets shall hereafter be made within any such subdivision by any
owner or owners or his or their agent until the plans for the subdivision and
the plans for improvements thereto have been reviewed and approved by the
Village Board of Trustees.
   D.   Subdivision of land lying outside of the Village and within one and
one-half (11/2) miles of the Village limits shall also be required to conform
with the requirements herein in accordance with the provisions of the "Revised
Cities and Villages Act" of the State of Illinois.
   E.   All interpretations of these rules and regulations are reserved to the
Village President and Board of Trustees.
   F.   The Village Board of Trustees may vary and make exceptions as set forth
herein in instances where there is sufficient evidence, in its opinion, of
hardship caused by topographic conditions or where any other reasonable
deterrents prevail.
   G.   Whenever a parcel is divided into lots containing one to five (5)
acres, inclusive, and there are indications that such lots will eventually be
resubdivided into smaller building lots, consideration shall be given to the
street and lot arrangement of the original subdivision so that additional minor
streets can be opened which will permit a logical arrangement of smaller lots.
(Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-1-6: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Notice Of Violation: Any person, firm or corporation found to be
violating any provision of this title shall be served by the Village with
written notice stating the nature of the violation and providing a reasonable
time limit for the satisfactory correction thereof. The offender shall, within
the period of time stated in such notice, permanently cease all violations.
(Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
   B.   Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation who shall continue any
violation beyond the time limit provided in subsection A of this section shall,
upon conviction thereof, be fined not more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00) for each violation. Each day in which any such violation shall
continue shall be deemed a separate offense. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991; amd. 2019
Code)
   C.   Liability For Costs And Damages: Any person, firm or corporation
violating any of the provisions of this title shall become liable to the
Village for any expense, loss or damage occasioned the Village by reason of
such violation. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
CHAPTER 2
RULES AND DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
11-2-1: Rules Of Word Construction
11-2-2: Definitions
11-2-1: RULES OF WORD CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Words used in the present tense shall include the future; words used in
the singular number shall include the plural number, and the plural the
singular.
   B.   The word "shall" is mandatory and not discretionary; the word "may" is
permissive.
   C.   The word "building" shall include the word "structure", and the word
"lot" shall include the word "plot". (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-2-2: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this title, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ALLEY: A public right-of-way, used primarily for vehicular traffic, along the
side of or in the rear of properties which affords only a secondary means of
access to these properties.
BLOCK: A tract of land bounded by streets, or a combination of streets, and
public parks, cemeteries, railroad rights-of- way, bulkhead lines or shorelines
of waterways, or corporate boundary lines of the Village.
BUILDING: Any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls used or
intended to be used for the shelter or enclosure of persons, animals,
equipment, machinery, or materials.
BUILDING LINE: A line within a lot or other parcel of land so designated on the
plat of the proposed subdivision, between which and the adjacent boundary of
the street or side upon which the lot abuts, the erection of an enclosed
structure or portion thereof is to be prohibited.
CROSSWALK: A strip of land dedicated to public use which is reserved across a
block to provide pedestrian access to adjacent areas.
CUL-DE-SAC: A street having one open end and being permanently terminated by a
vehicle turnaround.
EASEMENT: A grant by a property owner for the use of a strip of land by the
general public, a corporation or a certain person or persons for a specific
purpose or purposes.
LOT: A single parcel of land which may be legally described as such or two (2)
or more adjacent numbered lots or parts of such lots in a recorded subdivision
plat having principal frontage on a street which comprises a site occupied by,
or intended for occupancy by, one principal use, together with accessory
buildings and uses, yards and other open spaces required by this title.
LOT, DOUBLE FRONTAGE: A lot which has a pair of opposite lot lines along two
(2) substantially parallel streets and which is not a corner lot.
MARGINAL ACCESS STREET: A minor street which is parallel to and adjacent to
primary streets and highways and which provides access to abutting properties
and protection to local traffic from fast, through moving traffic on the
primary streets.
MINOR STREET: A street intended primarily as access to abutting properties.
OFFICIAL MAP: The approved Official Map of the Village of Chebanse, Illinois.
PARKWAY: A route intended to be used primarily by passenger vehicles and whose
right-of-way is or is intended to be developed in a parklike character.
PLAT: A plan, map, drawing or chart on which the subdivider's plan of the
subdivision is presented and which he submits for approval and intends to
record in final form.
PLAT, FINAL: The drawings and documents presented for final approval and as
described in chapter 4 of this title.
PLAT, PRELIMINARY (GENERAL PLAN): The drawings and documents presented for
conditional approval and as described in chapter 4 of this title.
PRIMARY OR MAJOR STREET: A street of considerable continuity which serves or is
intended to serve as a major traffic artery connecting large areas.
PROTECTIVE SCREEN PLANTING: A planting of trees, shrubs and/or evergreens
bordering an area intended to reduce and/or eliminate the nuisance of sound and
sight of adjoining uses.
PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT: Any improvement for the benefit of the public, financed and
executed by any interest, public or private.
PUBLIC STREET: All primary, secondary and minor streets which are shown on the
subdivision plat and are to be dedicated for public use.
ROADWAY: The paved area for vehicular traffic existing on a street right-of-way
and not the street right-of-way width.
SECONDARY OR COLLECTOR STREET: A street which carries traffic from minor
streets to the primary street system, including the principal entrance streets
of a residence development and streets for circulation within such development.
STREET: An area which serves, or is intended to serve, as a vehicular and
pedestrian access to abutting lands or to other streets.
STREET WIDTH: The shortest distance between lines of lots delineating the
public street.
STRUCTURE: That which is built or constructed, an edifice or building of any
kind, or any piece of work artificially built up or composed of parts joined
together in some definite manner.
SUBDIVIDER: The person or persons, group or corporation acting as a unit, or
any agent thereof, responsible for preparing and recording the plats of the
subdivision and for carrying out all appropriate requirements relating thereto
as outlined in this title.
SUBDIVISION: The division of land into two (2) or more parts, any of which is
less than five (5) acres, for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of
transfer of ownership or building development, including all public streets,
alleys, ways for public service facilities, parks, playgrounds, school grounds
or other public grounds, and all the tracts, parcels, lots or blocks, and
numbering of all such lots, blocks or parcels by progressive numbers, giving
their precise dimensions; provided, however, that the following shall not be
considered a subdivision and shall be exempt from the requirements herein:
   A.   The division or subdivision of land into parcels or tracts of five (5)
acres or more in size which does not involve any new streets or easements of
access.
   B.   The division of lots or blocks of less than one acre in any recorded
subdivision which does not involve any new streets or easements of access.
   C.   The sale or exchange of parcels of land between owners of adjoining and
contiguous land.
   D.   The conveyance of parcels of land or interests therein for use as
right-of-way for railroads or other public utility facilities which does not
involve any new streets or easements of access.
   E.   The conveyance of land owned by a railroad or other public utility
which does not involve any new streets or easements of access.
   F.   The conveyance of land for highway or other public purposes or grants
or conveyances relating to the dedication of land for public use or instruments
relating to the vacation of land impressed with a public use.
   G.   Conveyances made to correct descriptions in prior conveyances.
   H.   The sale or exchange of parcels or tracts of land existing on October
7, 1991, into no more than two (2) parts and not involving any new street or
easements of access.
VILLAGE ENGINEER: The person or firm charged with the responsibility of
Municipal engineering matters.
VILLAGE PRESIDENT AND BOARD OF TRUSTEES: Whenever the words "Board",
"Trustees", "Village Board of Trustees", or "Village Board" are used in this
title, they shall mean the Village President and Board of Trustees of the
Village of Chebanse, Illinois.
ZONING ORDINANCE: The zoning ordinance of the Village of Chebanse, Illinois.
(Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
CHAPTER 3
DESIGN STANDARDS AND REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
11-3-1: Design Standards For Public Ways
11-3-2: Sewer System
11-3-3: Water System
11-3-4: Street And Area Lighting
11-3-5: Easements
11-3-1: DESIGN STANDARDS FOR PUBLIC WAYS:
The subdivision of land, including the arrangement, character, extent, width,
grade and location of all streets, alleys or other land to be dedicated for
public use, shall conform to accepted and general Municipal practices and to
the Official Map of the Village as approved and adopted by the Village Board;
and shall be considered in their relation to existing and planned streets, to
topographical conditions, to public convenience and safety, and in their
appropriate relation to the proposed uses of the land to be served by such
streets. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991; amd. 2019 Code)
   A.   Location Of Streets And Walks:
      1.   Each lot or parcel of ground within a new subdivision shall be
adjacent to a public street.
      2.   The street system in each new subdivision shall continue and extend
existing connecting streets in adjoining subdivisions except minor streets
across a major intervening street where such continuation or extension is not
necessary to protect the interests of the public.
      3.   The street system in each new subdivision shall be extended and
dedicated to any adjacent unsubdivided property except in those instances in
which the adjacent property is not capable of being subdivided.
      4.   No street shall be located less than three hundred forty feet (340')
from any parallel street measured at the centerline of the streets, and the
other two (2) streets completing the block shall not be more than one thousand
three hundred twenty feet (1,320') measured at the centerlines of the streets,
except in those instances in which the topography of the land being subdivided
or the physical situation of that land, in the opinion of the Village Board,
makes such a street arrangement impractical.
      5.   Whenever two (2) parallel streets are located more than seven
hundred fifty feet (750') apart, a public walk having a right-of-way of not
less than ten feet (10') in width shall be provided for pedestrian travel to
schools, playgrounds, shopping centers, and other community facilities. Each
such public walk shall be located approximately equal distances between the two
(2) parallel streets and shall not contain any offsets from one street to the
other. These public walks shall be lighted in accordance with section
11-3-4 of this chapter.
      6.   No private streets will be permitted except for special developments
as may be set forth in the Village zoning ordinance.
      7.   Where a proposed subdivision borders on a present or proposed
Federal, State or limited access highway, traffic service to the proposed
subdivision bordering such highway shall be provided by a marginal access
street. Access to these types of highways from the marginal access street or
proposed subdivision proper shall be at one-half (1/2) mile intervals, unless
the proposed subdivision frontage is less than one-half (1/2) mile, in which
case, the proposed subdivision shall have only one access point to the highway
at a location recommended by the Village President and Board of Trustees.
The marginal access street shall be approximately parallel to and at a distance
suitable for the appropriate use of the intervening land for platted lots
facing the marginal access street, or for parkway purposes in Residential
Districts, or for parking in Commercial or Industrial Districts. Such distances
shall be determined with due regard for the requirements of approach grades and
possible future grade separations.
      8.   Sidewalks shall be constructed on both sides of every street facing
lots in accordance with applicable regulations of the Village for the
construction of public sidewalks.
      9.   All public walks designed for pedestrian travel shall be improved
with not less than four inches (4") of portland cement concrete pavement to a
width not less than four feet (4'), except where a greater thickness is
required by the regulations of the Village for the construction of public
sidewalks, there must be compliance with such regulations (see section
11-5-1 of this title for figure).
   B.   Design Of Streets:
      1.   The minimum width of right-of-way for streets shall be as follows:
         a.   Major streets, being those streets used primarily for through
traffic including those designated as such by the Corporate Authorities of the
Village, shall conform to the specifications shown in the current Highway
Standards and/or Design Manual, both published by the Department of
Transportation of the State of Illinois, and as the same may be hereafter
amended, but under no condition will the right- of-way be less than eighty feet
(80'). These current Highway Standards and Design Manual and any revisions or
amendments which may from time to time be made are hereby adopted and made a
part of this section to the same extent and with the same legal effects as if
fully set forth herein.
         b.   All other streets, including those designated by the Corporate
Authorities of the Village as secondary or nonarterial streets, shall be
platted to a width of not less than sixty feet (60').
      2.   Whenever a street in a new subdivision is a continuation of an
existing street in an adjoining subdivision and the right-of-way of the
existing street is less than the applicable width prescribed in subsection B1
of this section, then the narrower right-of-way may be continued into the new
subdivision if the interests of the public are not adversely affected.
      3.   Whenever a street in a new subdivision is a permanent street and is
not and cannot be continued to another street, the street shall be provided
with a permanent turnaround, the right-of-way for which shall be not less than
one hundred feet (100') in diameter.
      4.   In each instance in which the subdivider owns the land on both sides
of a proposed street, the entire right-of-way for the street shall be dedicated
by the subdivider.
      5.   When a new subdivision adjoins a dedicated half street in an
existing subdivision, the subdivider shall dedicate the remainder of the
street.
      6.   In those instances in which the owner or owners of a new subdivision
own the land on only one side of an existing street, the right-of-way of which
is narrower than that required by subsection B1 of this section, the subdivider
shall dedicate additional right-of-way of sufficient width to make that portion
of the right-of-way lying between the centerline of the existing right-of-way
and the outside edge of the additional right-of-way at least equal to one-half
(1/2) the required right-of-way width.
      7.   Major streets may be designed with gradual curves having a
centerline radius of at least five hundred feet (500') except where a lesser
radius is deemed safe and adequate to serve the public needs. All other streets
may be designed with gradual curves having a centerline radius of at least one
hundred fifty feet (150') except where a lesser radius is deemed safe and
adequate to serve the public needs. No streets shall be laid out with jogs
having centerline offsets of less than one hundred twenty five feet (125').
      8.   Cul-de-sacs shall have a maximum length of three hundred feet (300')
measured from the centerline of the intersecting street to the center of the
turnaround unless the topography of the land being subdivided or the physical
situation of that land makes such a restriction impractical.
   C.   Location And Design Of Alleys:
      1.   Alleys shall be provided for lots or parcels of ground intended for
business, commercial, or industrial uses unless the development plan for such
eliminates their need.
      2.   Alleys may be provided for all lots or parcels of ground intended
for multiple-family residential use.
      3.   No alley shall be provided for lots intended for one- and two-family
residential uses.
      4.   The minimum width of right-of-way for alleys shall be as follows:
         a.   Alleys to serve business, commercial or industrial uses: Twenty
four feet (24').
         b.   Alleys to serve multiple-family residential area only: Twenty
feet (20').
      5.   No dead end alleys will be permitted.
      6.   No private alleys will be permitted.
   D.   Names Of Streets And Alleys:
      1.   Proposed streets which are obviously in alignment with or
continuations of existing streets already named shall bear the same name as the
existing streets. In no case shall the name of the proposed new street
duplicate the name of an existing street in the Village.
      2.   Alleys shall not be named.
   E.   Construction Of Streets, Alleys And Walks:
      1.   The grades of major streets shall not be steeper than three percent
(3.0%). The grades of all other streets shall not be steeper than five percent
(5.0%). No tangent street grades shall be less than 0.4 percent.
      2.   All streets other than existing streets, all alleys and all public
walks for pedestrian travel shall be graded and the surface thereof improved as
herein provided (see section
11-5-1 of this title for figure). Street improvements shall be bounded by
combination curbs and gutters (see sections
11-5-1 and
11-5-2 of this title for figures).
      3.   The minimum width of improved areas of streets shall be as follows:
         a.   Major streets: Width as shown in the current Highway Standards
and/or Design Manual of the Department of Transportation of the State of
Illinois. The current Highway Standards and Design Manual are referred to in
subsection B1a of this section, and the adopting clause is applied equally to
this subsection E3a. See also subsection E5 of this section.
         b.   All other streets: See subsection E6 of this section, and see
section
11-5-1 of this title for figure.
         c.   The outside diameter of the surfaced area of the permanent
turnaround at the end of a cul-de-sac shall not be less than eighty feet (80').
      4.   The minimum width of improved areas of alleys shall be as follows:
         a.   Alleys to serve business, commercial and industrial areas or
uses: Twenty feet (20').
         b.   Alleys to serve multiple-family areas or uses: Sixteen feet
(16').
      5.   Pavements for major streets and streets in areas intended for
business, commercial or industrial uses shall be constructed with either
portland cement concrete or bituminous concrete in accordance with existing
specifications of the Department of Transportation of the State of Illinois.
The pavements for these streets shall be designed in accordance with the
appropriate section or sections of the Design Manual, the Highway Design
Standards or Flexible Pavement Design, all three (3) as published by the
Department of Transportation of the State of Illinois. The designer shall, with
assistance from the Department of Transportation and Village Engineer, estimate
the type and number of vehicles per day for a design period of twenty (20)
years from which the pavement structure thickness and the pavement width will
be determined. Alley pavements to serve business, commercial and industrial
areas shall conform to major street pavement requirements. In the absence of
adequate soil analysis, a soil support (IBR) value of 2.0 shall be used.
      6.   All other streets shall be designed and constructed in the same
manner as designated in subsection E5 of this section; except, that the minimum
thickness shall be three inches (3") of asphaltic concrete laid in two (2)
courses, upon an aggregate base eight inches (8") in thickness, or a lime
stabilized base ten inches (10") in thickness, or an unreinforced portland
cement concrete pavement seven inches (7") in thickness. (See section
11-5-1 of this title for figure.)
      7.   All curb corners shall have a radius of not less than twenty feet
(20'), and at intersections involving major streets, such radii shall be not
less than twenty five feet (25').
      8.   All public walks designed for pedestrian travel shall be improved
with not less than four inches (4") of portland cement concrete pavement to a
width of at least four feet (4') (see section
11-5-1 of this title for figure). (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
      9.   All streets shall be provided with catch basins and underground
drainage facilities having a design capacity adequate to carry off surface
water falling or coming on the streets in a 5-year storm as that term is used
in publications of the State Water Survey, Illinois Department of Natural
Resources, Office of Water Resources (IDNR/OWR). Sufficient inlets shall be
provided so that no pavement is designed to allow water to drain across the
crown of an intersecting street or is carried in the gutter for more than four
hundred feet (400'). Storm sewer systems shall be constructed with bell and
spigot or tongue and groove pipe of such type as required to provide adequate
strength for the load to be carried. The proposed storm sewer system must be in
conformance with the "Proposed Storm Sewer System for Chebanse, Illinois",
which is on file with the Village Clerk, and as approved by the Village
Engineer. For further stormwater handling design criteria, see article A of
this chapter. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991; amd. 2019 Code)
      10.   The subdivider shall notify the Village Clerk and the Village
inspector in advance of the date construction of the required improvements will
begin.
      11.   No plan of any subdivision shall be finally approved by the Village
Board of Trustees until:
         a.   A copy of the plans and specifications for the required street,
alley and public walk improvements, including street drainage, has been filed
with and approved by the Village Board of Trustees. The plans and
specifications shall meet the minimum design standards that are on file in the
Office of the Village Clerk.
         b.   The improvements (including the street drainage) have actually
been constructed in accordance with such plans and specifications or a surety
bond payable to the Village in a penal sum equal to at least fifty dollars
($50.00) per linear foot of street pavement, conditioned upon the construction
of the improvements in full conformity with the plans and specifications within
two (2) years from the date thereof, and with surety thereon satisfactory to
the Village President and Board of Trustees, has been filed with the Village
Clerk. Any bond so given to guarantee the construction of any such improvement
may be released by the Village President and Board of Trustees only after
receiving a written statement from the Village Clerk that the improvement has
been constructed and that the certificate of a registered professional engineer
as required in subsection E11c of this section has been received.
         c.   A certificate of a registered professional engineer employed by
the subdivider is filed with the Village Clerk certifying that the required
improvements were inspected during actual construction by such registered
professional engineer or some competent person acting under his direction and
that such improvements have been constructed in accordance with the aforesaid
plans and specifications; or in the event the subdivider files a bond as
provided in subsection E11b of this section, provision guaranteeing such
inspection during construction as required herein and the furnishing of the
aforesaid certificate of the registered professional engineer upon completion
of construction of the required improvements. In the event the engineer
employed by the subdivider is discharged before completion of the required
improvements, an amendment to the existing bond naming the new registered
professional engineer shall be filed with the Village and approved before
proceeding any further with the construction of the required improvements.
      12.   A four-way metal street sign shall be erected at each street
intersection. Such signs shall conform to the specifications on file in the
Village Clerk's Office.
      13.   All lot corners shall be monumented by at least a one- half inch
(1/2") diameter round or one-half inch (1/2") square iron rod or one-half inch
(1/2") iron pipe at least thirty inches (30") long set on the lot corner. All
lot corners that may have been disturbed or lost during construction of streets
and sewers shall be replaced at the expense of the subdivider. All block
corners, beginning and ending of all curves on curved streets or angle points
in streets, shall be monumented with a permanent monument set in a concrete
post; the concrete post having a minimum cross section of a four inch (4")
diameter circle. This monument shall be set sufficiently below the surface of
the ground to make its disturbance unlikely. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-3-2: SEWER SYSTEM:
   A.   Public System:
      1.   No plat of any new subdivision shall be approved by the Village
Board of Trustees unless the same provides for, and assures the construction by
the subdivider of, a sanitary sewage collection system which shall be adequate
to serve the needs of the entire subdivision when the same is fully developed.
The location and design of the system shall be approved by the Village Board of
Trustees and the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency.
      2.   No plat of any new subdivision shall be approved by the Village
Board of Trustees unless the same provides for and assures adequate treatment
of all sewage for the entire subdivision when the same is fully developed. The
location and design of the treatment facilities, if other than that provided by
the Village, shall be approved by the Village Board of Trustees and the
Illinois Environmental Protection Agency.
   B.   Private System:
      1.   If the developer requests approval for the use of individual septic
tanks as a method of treatment, the developer shall provide percolation test
data at a minimum frequency of one test hole for each lot in the approximate
areas of the proposed absorption field. The use of such septic tanks as a
method of treatment must be approved by the Village Board of Trustees and the
Kankakee County or Iroquois County Health Department and, if approved, shall be
installed using the latest plans and specifications on file with the Kankakee
County or Iroquois County Health Department.
      2.   If the developer's request for use of individual septic tanks is
granted, the developer shall provide a set of preliminary plans for a sewage
collection system that will adequately serve the needs for the entire
development. These preliminary plans shall show locations of manholes,
cleanouts, sewer line sizes, flow line elevations with grades and all other
information that is normally shown on such a preliminary plan. (Ord. 91-6, 10-
7-1991)
11-3-3: WATER SYSTEM:
   A.   System Required; Location And Design: No plat of any new subdivision
shall be approved by the Village Board of Trustees unless the same provides for
and assures the construction by the subdivider of a water distribution system
which will be adequate to serve the needs of the entire subdivision when the
same is fully developed; except, that no water main shall be less than six
inches (6") in diameter. The location and design of the system shall be
approved by the Village Board of Trustees, the Village Engineer and the
Illinois Environmental Protection Agency. The water distribution system shall
be in conformance with the "Proposed Water System Improvements for Chebanse,
Illinois", which is on file with the Village Clerk.
   B.   Hydrants: The developer shall provide fire hydrants of the type and
style now in use by the Village throughout the entire subdivision with one fire
hydrant at each street intersection and others spaced not more than four
hundred feet (400') apart or as approved by the Village Board of Trustees and/
or the Village Fire Department or Fire Marshal.
   C.   Valves And Valve Boxes: The developer shall provide valves with valve
boxes throughout the entire subdivision in such a manner that large sections of
the subdivision need not be shut down while repairs in other locations within
the development are being carried out.
   D.   As Built Plans: Upon completion of the installation of the water
distribution system, a set of as built plans shall be filed with the Village
Clerk. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-3-4: STREET AND AREA LIGHTING:
   A.   No plat of any new subdivision will be approved by the Village
President and Board of Trustees unless same provides for street (area) lighting
by any of the following means:
      1.   By use of luminaires which shall be either mercury vapor or sodium
vapor. The poles shall be polished aluminum with aluminum bracket arms. The
poles shall be spaced approximately two hundred fifty feet (250') apart such
that the average horizontal foot-candles shall be a minimum of 0.2. The design
and installation shall be in accordance with the current minimum standards as
set forth by the American Society of Illuminating Engineers. Wooden poles will
not be allowed nor will bracket arms secured to existing wooden utility poles
be allowed.
      2.   By requiring in covenants covering the subdivision that the owners
of every lot shall erect and maintain one yard light located in the front yard.
Each yard light shall be approximately six feet (6') in height, be equipped
with a photoelectric cell that illuminates the light during the hours of
darkness and be such that a seventy five (75) to one hundred (100) watt
incandescent light bulb can be safely used.
      3.   Any other means which is in accordance with current minimum
standards as set forth by the American Society of Illuminating Engineers.
   B.   Final selection for lighting is to be approved by the Village President
and Board of Trustees.
   C.   Upon completion of the installation of the street (area) lighting
system, a set of as built plans shall be filed with the Village Clerk. If
street (area) lighting is to be provided by individual front yard lights, as
built plans will not be required. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-3-5: EASEMENTS:
   A.   Nature Gas Main Easements:
      1.   No plat of any new subdivision will be approved by the Village Board
of Trustees unless the same provides for the necessary easements, if the
proposed street rights-of-way are not being utilized, for the installation of
natural gas mains. The developer shall provide the Village President and Board
of Trustees plans for these gas mains as proposed by the gas utility company.
      2.   Upon completion of the installation of the natural gas mains, a set
of as built plans shall be filed with the Village Clerk.
   B.   Electric, Telephone And Cable TV Easements:
      1.   No plat of any new subdivision will be approved by the Village
President and Board of Trustees unless the same provides for the necessary
easements for the installation of underground electricity, underground
telephone service, underground cable TV service or any other utility not
previously covered in this title. The developer shall provide the Village Board
of Trustees plans for these underground utilities as proposed by the utility
company. Aerial facilities will not be allowed for electric, telephone or cable
TV facilities.
      2.   Upon completion of the installation of the underground electric,
telephone, cable TV, etc., a set of as built plans for each utility shall be
filed with the Village Clerk. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
ARTICLE A. STORMWATER CONTROL
SECTION:
11-3A-1: Definitions
11-3A-2: Compliance With Village Guidelines
11-3A-3: Standards Of Determining Adequacy Of Stormwater Control
11-3A-4: Stormwater Management Policy Guidelines
11-3A-4-1: Purpose, Intent And Interpretation
11-3A-4-2: Scope
11-3A-4-3: Technical Requirements
11-3A-4-4: General Requirements
11-3A-4-5: Submittals
11-3A-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and terms, as used in this article, shall have the
following meanings unless the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
DETENTION FACILITIES: Facilities that provide for temporary storage of
stormwater runoff in basins, on rooftops, in parking lots, in lakes, in ponds,
or in other areas, and which control the release of this runoff with the
appropriately installed device during and after a flood or storm.
DOMESTIC SEWAGE: Water and water carried wastes normally discharged into the
sanitary sewers from dwellings, including single-family homes, multiple-family
homes and hotels, from office buildings, factories and institutions, but not
including stormwater drainage or surface water drainage and not including
industrial wastes, as defined in this section.
DRY BOTTOM DETENTION STORAGE: A detention facility that is designed to be
normally dry and which accumulates excess stormwater during a flood or storm.
INDUSTRIAL USER: Any nongovernmental user of the Village sewage system,
including agriculture, forestry, fishing, mining, manufacturing,
transportation, communication, electric, gas and sanitary services and any
other industrial services discharging into the Village sanitary sewer system
any industrial waste, or discharging into the Village sanitary sewer system any
wastes other than domestic sewage, as defined in this section.
INDUSTRIAL WASTES: All water, water carried solids, liquid and gas wastes
resulting from any industrial, manufacturing or food processing operation or
process or from the development of any natural resource, or any mixture of
these fluids and domestic sewage, or any mixture of these fluids with any other
water or with any other liquid.
OWNER: The owner, tenant, occupant or person in charge of any building or
premises, or any person acting in the owner's behalf.
PERSON: Any person, firm, corporation or association.
PUBLIC SANITARY SEWER: Any sanitary sewer constructed by the Village or
dedicated to the Village, regardless of the source of funding, and any sanitary
sewer belonging to any public trust or Municipal corporation or body politic of
any kind.
RETENTION FACILITIES: A facility designed to completely retain a specified
amount of stormwater runoff without gravity release. Retention basins are
generally considered an inappropriate technique for managing stormwater in the
area of Chebanse. The construction of retention basins is not required or
advocated by this article.
RUNOFF: The amount of rainfall that flows directly or indirectly into the storm
sewer system of the Village.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer that conveys sewage and wastewater in which ordinarily
groundwater and unpolluted industrial wastes are not included.
STORMWATER RUNOFF: The water that results from precipitation which is not
absorbed by soil or plant material, which does not evaporate and which flows
over the surface of the ground or is collected in channels, conduits or ponds.
SUBSIDIARY DRAINAGE PLAT: The topographical and profile studies signed by the
owner or his duly authorized attorney and a registered professional engineer,
and is submitted with a plat to meet the requirements of the Plat Act 1 . The
Village will not file the subsidiary drainage plat with the final plat but will
maintain a copy in its files in accordance with the Plat Act.
SURFACE WATER DRAINAGE: The movement of water upon whatever surface that is
exposed to the sky, as opposed the movement of groundwater or water in pipes.
WASTEWATER: Sewage.
WASTEWATER PLANT: Any facility owned by the Village used for receiving and
treating sewage.
WATERSHED: The land area above a given point on the ground that contributes
stormwater to that point.
WET BOTTOM DETENTION STORAGE: A detention facility that contains a body of
water and which accumulates excess stormwater during a flood or storm. (Ord.
04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
 
Notes
1 1. 765 ILCS 205/2.
11-3A-2: COMPLIANCE WITH VILLAGE GUIDELINES:
The Village President and Board of Trustees requires that all improvements
"conform with local, State, and Federal authorities which have jurisdiction
over the subdivision". Therefore, the design for stormwater control shall
conform to the technical guidelines set out in this article. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-
1991; amd. 2019 Code)
11-3A-3: STANDARDS OF DETERMINING ADEQUACY OF STORMWATER CONTROL:
Standards for determining the adequacy of provisions for the collection and
diversion of surface waters and calculations required to be made and provided
the Village Engineer are as follows: A subsidiary drainage plat shall be
submitted simultaneously with the subdivision plat, which shall show
topographically and by profile the elevation of the land prior to the
commencement of any change in elevations as a part of any phase of subdivision,
and additionally, if it is contemplated that such elevations, or the flow of
surface water from such land, will be changed as a result of any portion of the
development, then such map shall also show such proposed changes in the
elevations and the flow of the surface water from such land. This topographical
and profile map which is to be submitted with the subdivision plat shall have
on its face the certification of a registered professional engineer and the
owner of the land to the effect that to the best of their knowledge and belief,
the drainage of surface waters will not be changed by the construction of such
subdivision or any part thereof, or that if such surface water drainage shall
be changed, adequate provision has been made for collection and diversion of
such surface waters into public areas or drains which the subdivider has the
right to use, and that such surface waters will not be deposited on the
property of adjoining landowners in such concentrations as may cause damage to
the adjoining property because of the concentration of the subdivision's
stormwater. (Ord. 04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
11-3A-4: STORMWATER MANAGEMENT POLICY GUIDELINES:
11-3A-4-1: PURPOSE, INTENT AND INTERPRETATION:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this section
11-3A-4 is to guide developers in attempts to control the transportation or
movement of stormwater, reduce damage to property and protect the public
health, safety, and general welfare.
   B.   Intent: The intent of this section
11-3A-4 is to require temporary storage of stormwater runoff and to control the
rate of release of stormwater runoff by interpretation of reasonable provisions
and in accordance with generally accepted engineering practices.
   C.   Interpretation: This section
11-3A-4 shall be interpreted to protect the public health, safety, and welfare
and shall not prevent the Village Engineer from determining that other or
additional requirements must be satisfied in order to promote the intent and
purpose hereof. (Ord. 04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
11-3A-4-2: SCOPE:
   A.   A combination of stormwater storage and controlled release is required
for all subdivisions involving:
      1.   Development greater than three (3) lots or one acre in area
including one-half (1/2) of existing adjacent streets; or less than one acre in
area with greater than fifty percent (50%) impervious surface area existing or
proposed improvements.
      2.   In any other development if the Village Engineer determines that the
development needs detention to prevent its doing harm.
   B.   Existing land uses, particularly agricultural, may be exempt if current
stormwater provisions do not adversely affect the servient estates. (Ord. 04-
14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
11-3A-4-3: TECHNICAL REQUIREMENTS:
The following requirements shall be applicable and shall be satisfied prior to
Village Engineer approval of the subsidiary drainage plat. No development shall
be authorized in the Village unless there is an adequate outlet and the Village
has approved retention or detention facilities. The applicant shall show, by
his detailed calculations, that the proposed outlet and retention or detention
facilities are adequate, and the calculations must be acceptable to the
Village. In the event the Village determines the outlet is not adequate, the
developer shall construct any required retention or detention facilities to
meet the restriction created by the inadequate outlet. Such facilities shall be
designed based on the following: (Ord. 04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014; amd.
2019 Code)
   A.   Design Formula: Unless otherwise approved by the Village Engineer,
formulas to be used in connection with the calculation of runoff volumes and
allowable release rates reasonably expected from the minimum design storm shall
be the rational method as outlined in the latest Illinois Department of
Transportation Drainage Manual for total contributing areas between twenty (20)
acres and five (5) acres and the soil conservation hydrograph method for areas
greater than twenty (20) acres.
   B.   Design Table: For areas of development less than five (5) acres, the
following storage and release rates will be required:
 
Area (A) (In Acres) Required Storage Rate (V) (In Maximum Release Rate Allowed
                    Cu. Ft./Acre)                 (Q) (In cfs/Acre)
1                   10,700                        1.05
2                   9,100                         0.90
3                   7,800                         0.78
4                   6,900                         0.64
5                   6,200                         0.60
 
Note: Storage rates and release rates shall be interpolated for areas between
table values to the nearest 0.1 acre.
   C.   Minimum Design Storm:
      1.   Storage volume (V), when using the soil conservation hydrograph
method, will be determined from inflow hydrographs generated by the design
formula using a minimum design storm with a range of rainfall intensities
associated with an average recurrence interval of one hundred (100) years and
an assumed coefficient for the proposed postdevelopment land use.
      2.   Storage volume, when using the rational method, will be the volume
generated by the difference between average runoffs of 100-year rainfall
frequency in postdevelopment condition and 5-year rainfall frequency in
predevelopment condition, assuming such difference occurs for one hour. The
average discharge shall be half of the peak discharge calculated by the
rational method.
      3.   Allowable release rate (Q) will be determined by the design formula
using a minimum design storm with an average rainfall intensity associated with
an average recurrence interval of five (5) years for the storm period
calculated by the time of concentration, as outlined by the latest technical
letters of the Illinois State Water Survey for rainfall frequencies. Runoff
coefficients or CN numbers used shall reflect predeveloped condition of the
watershed. The predeveloped condition of the land shall be defined as
agricultural (straight row crop) or forested, as appropriate. For sites that
are being redeveloped from a use other than the defined predeveloped condition,
the Village may approve use of coefficients or CN numbers for the existing land
use only if the subservient drainage system has adequate capacity in accordance
with the current Village ordinances for flows from the existing site. (Ord. 04-
14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
11-3A-4-4: GENERAL REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Miscellaneous Requirements:
      1.   Where the proposed structure, project or land development forms only
a portion of a watershed or contains portions of several watersheds, the
storage volume calculations shall be based upon the area of the entire project,
development or land use change.
      2.   The storage of excess stormwater runoff from a 100-year return
period storm having a duration of twenty four (24) hours, released at the
allowable rate, shall not result in a storage duration in excess of twenty four
(24) hours, but storage duration may be as long as forty eight (48) hours or
more upon site specific approval by the Village. All design calculations must
be submitted to the Village Engineer for approval. The tabulated values in
section
11-3A-4-3 of this section
11-3A-4 accommodate this requirement.
      3.   Each stormwater storage area shall be provided with a method of
overflow in the event a storm in excess of the design capacity occurs. This
overflow facility shall be constructed to function without special maintenance
attention and can become a part of the excess stormwater passageway for the
entire development.
      4.   The entire stormwater storage area shall be designed and constructed
to fully protect the public health, safety and welfare. The minimum building
site elevation for wet or dry basins shall be set at a minimum of two feet (2')
above the maximum calculated storage elevation for the 100-year event. The
maximum elevation will include the energy head at the outfall structure. If a
condition occurs in the stormwater storage area which is hazardous to the
public health, safety or welfare, the property owner or owners shall provide
approved corrective measures. In the event these corrective measures are not
provided, the Village may eliminate the hazard at the expense of the property
owner or person responsible.
      5.   The stormwater storage area shall be designed with a minimum of
twelve inches (12") of freeboard above the calculated 100-year water surface
elevation.
   B.   Dry Bottom Stormwater Storage:
      1.   Dry bottom stormwater storage areas should be designed where
possible to serve a secondary purpose for recreation, open space, or similar
types of uses which will not be adversely affected by occasional intermittent
flooding and will not interfere with stormwater management. Backyard storage
will not normally be an approved method of controlling stormwater runoff. In
the event the Village determines that backyard storage is the only feasible
method of storage, extraordinary lot depth will be provided to afford the
property owner adequate recreational area use as determined by the Village
Engineer.
      2.   Minimum grades for longitudinal turf areas shall be one percent (1%)
(100 units horizontal to 1 unit vertical), and maximum side slopes shall be
thirty three percent (33%) (3 units horizontal to 1 unit vertical). Minimum
transverse bottom grade shall be one percent (1%). Storage area side slopes
shall follow the natural land contours as closely as practicable, and a minimum
of earth excavation shall be used to create the storage facility. Geometries of
dry bottom stormwater storage areas shall be approved by the Village Engineer.
      3.   Temporary seeding or other soil stabilization measures shall be
established in the stormwater storage area and the excess stormwater passageway
immediately following the construction or reconstruction of these areas. During
the construction of the overall development, it is recognized that a limited
amount of sediment buildup may occur in the stormwater storage areas due to
erosion. In no case shall the volume of the storage area be reduced to less
than ninety percent (90%) of the required design volume during the construction
phase of the development.
      4.   Permanent erosion control measures such as mulching, hydroseeding,
conventional seeding, nurse crops, fertilizing, or sod installation shall be
utilized to control soil movement and erosion within the storage area and the
excess stormwater passageway. These measures shall meet or exceed the standards
established by the Iroquois County or Kankakee County Soil and Water
Conservation District. The installation of these permanent measures shall take
place only after the majority of construction and other silt and sediment
producing activities have been completed. Prior to the final establishment of
the stormwater storage area and the excess stormwater passageway, all
dimensions and volumes shall be restored.
      5.   The outlet control structure shall be provided with an interceptor
for trash and debris, and it shall be designed and constructed to prevent soil
erosion and not require manual adjustments for its proper operation. The
control structure shall be designed to operate properly with little or no
maintenance or attention. The control structure shall be provided with safety
screens for any pipe or opening, other than a weir, to prevent children or
large animals from crawling into structures. The control structure shall be
constructed to allow access to it at all times, including times of flood flow.
      6.   Pipe outlets of less than ten inches (10") in diameter shall not be
allowed unless specifically approved by the Village Engineer. Multiple outlet
pipes from a storm storage area shall be avoided if they are designed to be
less than twelve inches (12") in diameter.
      7.   Maximum planned depth of stormwater stored shall not exceed four
feet (4').
      8.   Tile underdrains shall be provided in dry bottom stormwater storage
areas. These tile underdrains shall be so constructed that they will not
interfere with any secondary usage of the storage area. Tile underdrains shall
be so constructed so that they shall facilitate dewatering of the soils in the
stormwater storage area to avoid any marshy or saturated soil conditions. Tile
underdrain systems shall be combined with the low flow conduits system and
shall be as approved by the Village Engineer. If an underdrain and low flow
conduit system is shown by the property owner to be unfeasible, the Village may
approve the use of a low flow channel that does not interfere with secondary
usage of this storage area.
      9.   Posting of danger signs mounted at appropriate locations to warn of
deep water, possible flood conditions during storm periods and any other
dangers that exist to pedestrian and vehicular traffic shall be the sole
responsibility of the owner.
      10.   Adequate energy dissipation measures shall be provided at discharge
points into the basin. These measures may include stilling basins, riprap, and
other erosion control measures.
   C.   Wet Bottom Stormwater Storage: The following additional regulations
shall apply:
      1.   Wet bottom stormwater storage areas shall be designed in compliance
with all the regulations which are applicable and govern the construction of
dry bottom stormwater storage areas.
      2.   The water surface area of the permanent pool shall not exceed one-
fifth (1/5) of the area of the tributary watershed, or as approved by the
Village Engineer.
      3.   Minimum normal water depth, excluding safety ledges and slide
slopes, shall be six feet (6'). If fish are to be used to keep the pond clean,
at least one-fourth (1/4) of the pond area shall be a minimum of ten feet (10')
deep.
      4.   Facilities should be provided to lower the pond elevation by gravity
flow for cleaning purposes and shoreline maintenance.
      5.   The control structure for stormwater release should be designed to
operate at full design rate with only a small increase in water depth in order
to minimize the land surface wetted by frequent minor stormwater runoff
conditions.
      6.   The facility shall be provided with an edge system that protects
banks from erosion due to wind action and event flows.
      7.   The storage facility shall provide a safety ledge below the normal
water surface where the slope shall not exceed 3:1 (3 units horizontal to 1
unit vertical) to a depth of four feet (4').
   D.   Paved Stormwater Storage: Design and construction of the pavement base
must ensure that there is no pavement damage due to flooding. Control
structures in paved areas must be readily accessible for maintaining and
cleaning. Flow control devices will be required unless otherwise approved by
the Village Engineer.
   E.   Street Pavement Surface Ponding: Street pavement surface ponding shall
not exceed three inches (3") in depth in the gutter line under all rainfall
conditions up to and including the 100-year storm event. Open waterways such as
surface overflow swales shall be designed into the grading plan to receive all
excess stormwater runoff. Depressing the sidewalk across such overflow swales
to meet this requirement shall be acceptable.
   F.   Rooftop Stormwater Storage: Rooftop storage of excess stormwater shall
be designed and constructed to provide permanent control inlets and parapet
walls to contain excess stormwater. Adequate structural roof design must be
provided to ensure that roof deflection does not occur which could cause the
roofing material to fail and result in leakage. Overflow area must be provided
to ensure that the weight of stormwater will never exceed the structural
capacity of the roof.
   G.   Automobile Parking Lot Storage Areas: Automobile parking lots may be
designed to provide temporary detention storage on a portion of their surfaces.
Automobile parking facilities used to store excess stormwater may be
constructed having a maximum depth of stored stormwater of eight inches (8");
and these areas shall be located in the most remote, least used areas of the
parking facility. Design and construction of automobile parking in stormwater
areas must ensure that there is no damage to the parking facility surfacing due
to flooding, including damage to the subbase. Warning signs shall be mounted at
appropriate locations to warn of possible flood conditions during a storm
period.
   H.   Underground Stormwater Storage: Underground stormwater storage
facilities must be designed for easy access in order to remove accumulated
sediment and debris. These facilities must be provided with a positive gravity
outlet unless otherwise approved by the Village Engineer.
   I.   Tributary Flows: If the site being developed receives tributary flows
from dominant land which are passed through to subservient lands, the developer
shall provide for those flows as follows:
      1.   The developer shall provide a storm sewer outlet for the average 5-
year undeveloped event or a surface drainageway designed for the 25-year event,
with provisions in either case for the 100-year event so as not to cause damage
or a threat to public safety.
      2.   The developer may elect to pass the flows from dominant land through
a proposed detention basin. If the developer so elects, the allowable discharge
to the subservient land may not exceed the undeveloped condition in any storm
event. This requirement will most likely result in a staged discharge outlet.
The controlled release rate to the subservient storm sewer system shall not
exceed the 5-year undeveloped rate or the capacity of the subservient storm
sewer system, whichever is less. The uncontrolled release rate from this site
cannot exceed the 100-year undeveloped release from the dominant land, plus the
allowable release (5-year undeveloped event) from this site. At no time will
the release from the detention facility exceed the undeveloped condition in any
storm event.
      3.   If the orderly management of the stormwater runoff cannot be
achieved by passing the entire tributary area runoff through the stormwater
storage area, then the stormwater storage area may be constructed to exclude
the runoff from the tributary area originating outside of the area to be
developed by separation or rerouting of flows to bypass the proposed detention/
retention facilities.
      4.   Where the owner has a large tract of land upon which development is
to occur in several phases, the owner is encouraged to construct one stormwater
storage facility which is designed to provide for the needs of the entire
completed development, or be enlarged at later dates as additional portions of
the owner's lands are developed and as additional stormwater storage is
required due to that development.
      5.   Where portions of the owner's land are tributary to the same drain
for an outlet, but which are within two (2) or more tributary areas to that
drain, the owner may construct, upon site specific approval by the Village
Engineer, compensatory stormwater detention facilities within one tributary
area which offset the lack of construction of stormwater detention facilities
in another tributary area. Such compensatory storage shall be designed and
constructed such that the net effect of these facilities shall be to limit the
amount of stormwater runoff released into the drain to that which would have
occurred had stormwater detention facilities been constructed for all the
tributary areas.
Stormwater storage areas may be planned and constructed jointly by two (2) or
more landowners so long as compliance with this section
11-3A-4 is maintained.
   J.   Easements: Easements to the Village and/or any legal entity (homeowner
association, etc.) responsible for the maintenance of drainage facilities shall
be granted to further this section
11-3A-4. (Ord. 04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-19-2014)
11-3A-4-5: SUBMITTALS:
Two (2) copies of all stormwater detention or retention system designs shall be
submitted by the developer and his engineer for approval simultaneously with
the subsidiary drainage plat. All calculations shall be shown legibly on eight
and one-half inch by eleven inch (81/2" x 11") sheets of paper. The subdivision
name, engineer's firm, engineer's initials and date shall all be indicated. For
all detention systems, a plot or tabulation of storage volumes with
corresponding water surface elevations (stage storage table) and of the basin
outflow rates for those water surface (stage discharge) elevations shall be
furnished. These tabulations shall be listed for water surface elevation
intervals not exceeding one-half foot (0.5'). (Ord. 04-14, 7-19-2014, eff. 7-
19-2014)
CHAPTER 4
PLAT REQUIREMENTS AND PROCEDURE
SECTION:
11-4-1: Procedure
11-4-2: Preliminary Plat
11-4-3: Final Plat
11-4-1: PROCEDURE:
A. At least ten (10) days before the regular Village Board of Trustees meeting,
there shall be filed seven (7) copies of a preliminary plan for examination and
subsequent recommendations for approval or disapproval. If the proposed plan of
subdivision is not satisfactory as presented, the Village Board of Trustees may
permit the subdivider to make the changes and additions required to meet the
requirements of this chapter. If the plan of subdivision, as shown by the
preliminary plan, is finally disapproved, the original plan shall be returned
to the subdivider, with a written statement of reasons for such disapproval. If
the proposed plan of subdivision, as shown by the preliminary plan, shall
finally be approved, the original plat and one copy thereof shall be endorsed
as follows:
Tentative approval by the President and Board of Trustees of the Village of
Chebanse this       day of                , 20     .
                                               
                     President
The original copy of the plat so endorsed shall be filed with the Village
Clerk. The other copy thereof shall be returned to the subdivider.
   B.   Within twelve (12) months after receiving tentative approval of the
preliminary plat by the Village President and Board of Trustees, the original
and seven (7) copies of the final plat shall be submitted by the developer for
recommended final approval by the Village President and Board of Trustees.
Tentative approval of the preliminary plat shall become null and void unless
the final plat is submitted within the twelve (12) months as herein required.
   C.   Following final approval by the Village President and Board of
Trustees, the final plat, as approved, may be legally recorded in compliance
with the laws of the State. Approval of the final plat by the Village President
and Board of Trustees shall be null and void if the plat is not recorded within
ninety (90) days after the date of approval, unless application for extension
of time is made in writing during said ninety (90) day period to the Village
President and Board of Trustees and granted. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-4-2: PRELIMINARY PLAT:
The preliminary plat submitted to the Village Board of Trustees shall be drawn
to a scale of one hundred feet (100') or less to the inch and shall show the
following information:
   A.   The location of the property with respect to adjacent property and
streets. There shall also be included a location map at a suitable scale to
show all streets and public ways within the general area of the subdivider's
property.
   B.   All pertinent features such as existing structures to remain, streets,
railroads, water bodies, streams, and wooded areas that may influence the
design of the subdivision.
   C.   Existing and proposed contours based on the USGS datum at intervals of
two feet (2') or less, unless waived by the Planning Commission.
   D.   The name, location and width of all proposed streets.
   E.   The proposed location and width of all alleys, lots, setback lines,
utility easements, and areas to be reserved for public use.
   F.   Existing sanitary sewers, storm drains, and culverts within the tract
and immediately adjacent thereto. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
   G.   Proposed sites, if any, for multi-family dwellings, shopping centers,
places of worship, industry, or other nonpublic uses exclusive of single-family
dwellings. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991; amd. 2019 Code)
   H.   Proposed provisions for disposal of sanitary waste and stormwater
drainage.
   I.   The name(s) and address(es) of the owner(s) of land to be subdivided,
the name and address of the subdivider, if other than the owner, and the name
of the land surveyor and/or registered engineer.
   J.   The north point, scale and date.
   K.   The proposed name of the subdivision. (Ord. 91-6, 10-7-1991)
11-4-3: FINAL PLAT:
The final plat shall be clearly and legibly drawn to a scale of one hundred
feet (100') or less to the inch on tracing cloth or mylar with black waterproof
ink, or equivalent. The final plat and/or accompanying documents shall show the
following information:
   A.   Name of subdivision.
   B.   Approximate true north point, date and scale.
   C.   Names and signatures of the owner, subdivider, and land surveyor;
signature and seal of registered engineer on all engineering drawings.
   D.   The legal description of the property subdivided, with the surveyor's
certificate and seal to the effect that the plat represents a survey made by
him and that all monuments are set as shown.
   E.   The accurate location and description of all monuments.
   F.   All angular and linear data along the exterior boundaries of the
subdivision. Boundary bearings for subdivisions over one hundred thousand
(100,000) square feet in an area shall be measured with reference to the true
meridian.
   G.   Locations and widths of all streets and sidewalks, together with names
of streets.
   H.   Location, dimensions and status of all easements.
   I.   Lot lines with accurate dimensions.
   J.   Radii of all curves and lengths of arcs.
   K.   Sufficient data to determine readily the location and length of all
lines.
   L.   All lot and block numbers.
   M.   A copy of the plans and specifications for the required streets,
alleys, public walk improvements, sanitary sewers, storm sewers, water mains,
gas mains, underground electric, telephone and TV cables, and any other public
utility facility.
   N.   A certificate from a registered professional engineer employed by the
subdivider that all required streets, alleys, public walk improvements, water
mains, sanitary sewers, storm sewers, gas mains, underground electric,
telephone, TV cables, and any other public utility facilities have been
constructed in accordance with the plans and specifications as submitted or a
surety bond as required in subsection 11-3-1E11b of this title.
   O.   Provision shall be made on the face of the plat for approval of the
Village President and Board of Trustees as follows:
The proposed Final Plan of subdivision as shown on this plat and accompanying
documents has received final approval by the President and Board of Trustees of
the Village of Chebanse.
Dated this day       of                 , 20    .
PRESIDENT AND BOARD OF TRUSTEES OF THE VILLAGE OF CHEBANSE.
                                            
                  Village President
ATTEST:
                       
Village Clerk
